Profit from Debt Repaid Then Found Nonexistent Is Halal
Ruling with proof for halal profit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on profit from a debt that is later discovered nonexistent, and explain the talil (legal reasoning) based on the distinction between determinate and indeterminate property.

Core Idea
Profit from debt repaid then nonexistent is halal because the impurity of defective ownership does not affect in indeterminate property.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a key fiqhi scenario: a claimant demands a debt, the defendant pays, then both realize the debt never existed. Meanwhile, the claimant used the money and made profit. Is that profit permissible? The Hanafi ruling is clear: it is halal. This lesson unpacks the sophisticated reasoning (talil) behind this ruling, focusing on the concepts of defective ownership (milk fasid) and the nature of dirhams as indeterminate property (ghayr muta'ayyin).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The scenario: defendant pays a claimed debt, then both agree debt never existed; claimant made profit from the money. Ruling: profit is halal.
2
Trace the source of impurity
The impurity (khabuth) arises from defective ownership (fasād al-milk), not from usurpation. The debt was initially valid, then nullified by mutual agreement, making the substitute ownership defective.
3
Understand the distinction between determinate and indeterminate property
Dirhams (rupees) are considered indeterminate (ghayr muta'ayyin) because one dirham is like another. Impurity from defective ownership does not attach to indeterminate property.
4
Apply the principle
Since the money is indeterminate, the impurity does not affect it, so the profit is pure and halal.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may hold that profit from defective ownership must be given in charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مدعی نے مدعی علیہ پر مال کا دعوی کیا مدعی علیہ نے مال ادا کر دیا پھر دونوں نے با ہم سچائی سے کہا کہ مدعی علیہ پر کچھ مال نہ تھا حالانکہ مدعی نے ان دراہم سے نفع اٹھایا تو نفع حلال ہے

قال وكذا اذا ادعى على اخر ما لا فقضاه اياه ثم تصادقا انه لم يكن عليه شئى وقد ربح المدعي في الدراهم يطيب لـه الـربـح لان الخبث لفساد الملك ههنا لان الدين وجب بالتسمية ثم استحق بالتصادق وبدل المستحق مملوك فلا يعمل فيما لايتعين

ترجمہ اور اسی طرح اگر ایک نے دوسرے پر مال کا دعوی کیا پس مدعی علیہ نے مدعی کو ادا کر دیا پھر دونوں نے باہم سچائی کے ساتھ کہا کہ مدعی علیہ پر کچھ مال نہ تھا حالانکہ مدعی نے ان دراہم میں نفع اٹھایا ہے تو مدعی کے لئے نفع حلال ہے کیونکہ یہاں خبث فساد ملک کی وجہ سے ہے کیونکہ قرضہ مدعی کے دعوی کرنے سے واجب ہوا ہے پھر باہمی تصدیق سے یہ قرضہ مستحق ہو گیا ہے اور اس قرضہ مستقہ کا بدل مملوک ہے اس لئے خبث ان دراہم میں مؤثر نہ ہو گا جو متعین نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے دوسرے پر دعویٰ کیا کہ میرے تجھ پر ایک ہزار روپیہ ہیں لہذا تم ایک ہزار رو پیادا کرو ۔ پس مدعی علیہ نے ایک ہزار روپیہ مدعی کو ادا کر دیئے پھر دونوں اس پر متفق ہو گئے کہ مدعی مدعلی علیہ پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے حالانکہ اس عرصہ میں مدعی نے مدعی علیہ کی اس رقم سے نفع حاصل کر لیا تو یہ نفع مدعی علیہ کے لئے حلال ہے اس کا صدقہ کرنا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں خبث فساد ملک کی وجہ سے ہے اور فساد ملک کی وجہ سے خبث اس لئے ہے کہ مدعی کے ایک ہزار روپیہ کا دعوی کرتے وقت مدعی علیہ کے اقرار کی وجہ سے مدعی علیہ پر ایک ہزار روپیہ کا دین ( قرضہ ) واجب ہوا ہے اور دین ما وجب فی الزمہ کو کہتے ہیں پس جب مدعی علیہ نے مدعی کو ایک ہزار روپے ادا کئے اور مدعی نے ان پر قبضہ کیا تو یہ ایک ہزار روپیہ دین کا بدل ہے نہ کہ دین کیونکہ دین مال نہیں ہوتا بلکہ دین وہ حق ہوتا ہے جو مدیون کے ذمہ میں ثابت ہوتا ہے پھر جب مدعی اور مدعلی علیہ نے اس پر اتفاق کر لیا کہ مدعی علیہ پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے تو گویا دین مستحق ہو گیا ہے یعنی ایسا ہو گیا گویا دین پر کسی نے استحقاق کا دعوی کر کے اس کو لے لیا ہے پس جب دین مستحق ہو گیا تو اس کے بدل یعنی ایک ہزار روپے میں مدعی کی ملک فاسد ہو جائے گی اور مدعی پر اس ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض باندی خریدی پھر مشتری نے باندی پر اور بائع نے ثمن پر قبضہ کر لیا اس کے بعد باندی مستحق ہوگئی تو یہ ایک ہزار روپیہ بائع کا مملوک ہوگا لیکن مشتری کو واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا اسی طرح دین کا عوض ایک ہزار روپیہ دین کے مستحق ہونے کے بعد مدعی کا مملوک تو ہے مگر ملک فاسد ہے اور ملک فاسد سے جو نفع حاصل ہوتا ہے اس میں خبث ہوتا ہے پس مدعی نے ایک ہزار روپیہ سے جو نفع حاصل کیا ہے وہ خبث ہے مگر چونکہ روپیہ یعنی دراہم متعین کرنے کے باوجود متعین نہیں ہوتے اس لئے ان میں خبث مؤثر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ جو خبث فساد ملک کی وجہ سے پیدا ہوتا ہے وہ مالا تعین میں مؤثر نہیں ہوتا پس جب یہاں خبث مؤثر نہیں ہوا تو مدعی کے لئے وہ نفع حلال ہے اور اس کا صدقہ کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔
A claimant claimed property from the defendant, the defendant paid it, then both truthfully said that the defendant owed nothing, while the claimant made profit from those dirhams, so the profit is halal. He said: Similarly, if one claims property from another and he pays him, then they mutually affirm that nothing was owed to him, and the claimant made profit in the dirhams, the profit is pure for him, because the impurity here is due to defective ownership. The debt became obligatory by the claim, then it became legally claimable (mustahaqq) by mutual affirmation, and the substitute of the claimable property is owned, so it does not operate in what is not determinate. Translation: Similarly, if one claims property from another, then the defendant pays the claimant, then both truthfully say that the defendant owed nothing, while the claimant made profit from those dirhams, then the profit is halal for the claimant, because the impurity here is due to defective ownership, because the debt became obligatory by the claim, then it became mustahaqq by mutual affirmation, and the substitute of that mustahaqq debt is owned, so the impurity does not affect those dirhams which are not determinate. Explanation: The scenario is that a person claimed from another: 'I have a thousand rupees on you, so pay a thousand rupees.' The defendant paid a thousand rupees to the claimant. Then both agreed that the claimant did not have anything due on the defendant. In the meantime, the claimant made profit from the defendant's money. Then this profit is halal for the claimant, and it is not obligatory to give it in charity. Because the impurity here is due to defective ownership. The impurity due to defective ownership is because when the claimant claimed a thousand rupees, due to the defendant's admission, a debt of a thousand rupees became due on the defendant. 'Dayn' is that which is due in the liability. So when the defendant paid the claimant a thousand rupees and the claimant took possession, this thousand rupees is the substitute of the debt, not the debt itself, because the debt is not property but a right established in the liability. Then when the claimant and defendant agreed that nothing was due on the defendant, it is as if the debt became mustahaqq (claimed and taken) - as if someone claimed the debt and took it. So when the debt became mustahaqq, in its substitute (the thousand rupees) the claimant's ownership becomes defective (fasad al-milk). Then if the claimant bought a slave-girl with this thousand rupees, and the buyer took possession of the slave-girl and the seller took possession of the price, then the slave-girl becomes mustahaqq, then the thousand rupees become owned by the seller, but he must return them to the buyer. Similarly, the substitute of the debt (the thousand rupees) after the debt becomes mustahaqq is owned by the claimant but with defective ownership. Profit from defective ownership has impurity. So the profit the claimant made from the thousand rupees is impure. But because rupees (dirhams) are not determinate even if specified, the impurity does not affect them. Since the impurity does not affect, the profit is halal for the claimant and it is not obligatory to give it in charity.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah. It presents a case: A claimant (mad'ī) demands money from a defendant (mad'ī 'alayh), who pays. Later both agree the debt never existed. The claimant had made profit from the money. The ruling: The profit is halal. The reasoning (talil) is that the impurity (khabuth) here arises from defective ownership (fasād al-milk), not from usurpation. Because the debt was valid initially due to the claim, then became mustahaqq (claimable) when both agreed nothing was owed. The money paid is a substitute (badal) for the debt. After the debt is nullified, the ownership of the substitute becomes defective. However, dirhams are not determinate (ghayr muta'ayyin), so the impurity does not affect them. Therefore, profit from such indeterminate property is halal and does not require charity. This follows the principle from the previous lesson that shubha in indeterminate property is weaker.

Key Terms
دین (dayn): A debt or liability that is not yet a specific property but a right in the liability.
بدل (badal): Substitute; the specific items given in payment for a debt.
مستحق (mustahaqq): Claimed and taken; a debt that becomes subject to recovery.
ملک فاسد (milk fāsid): Defective ownership; ownership that is legally flawed but not void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the profit from the repaid money halal in this case?
A) Because the debt was valid initially, so the money was owned properly.
B) Because the impurity is due to defective ownership, and dirhams are indeterminate, so the impurity does not affect.
C) Because the claimant had good intentions.
D) Because the defendant agreed to give the money as a gift.

Key Takeaway
Profit from a debt repaid then found nonexistent is halal in the Hanafi school, because the impurity of defective ownership does not affect indeterminate property like dirhams.

The Prohibition of Najsh and Bidding on Another's Negotiation
Explains the prohibition of najsh and overbidding on a pending sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of najsh and bidding on another's negotiation, identify the underlying reason (harm and deceit), and distinguish when such actions are permissible (auction).

Core Idea
Najsh and overbidding on a settled deal are prohibited due to deceit and harm; auction is permissible when no prior agreement exists.

This passage from Ashraf ul-Hadaya explains two related prohibitions in sales. The Prophet (PBUH) forbade both najsh—artificially inflating prices without intent to buy—and bidding on a negotiation that has already been concluded. The underlying rationale is that such actions cause estrangement and harm. However, if the parties have not yet reached an agreement, competitive bidding (auction) is permissible. Understanding this distinction is essential for ethical commerce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Prohibitions
Locate the two actions prohibited by the hadith: najsh and bidding on another's negotiation (as-saum 'ala saum al-ghair).
2
Define Each Prohibition
Najsh is increasing the price without intending to buy. Bidding on another's negotiation refers to offering a higher price after the parties have mutually agreed on a sum.
The hadith explicitly links them with similar reasoning.
3
Understand the Illa (Reason)
The text states the prohibition is due to 'estrangement and harm' (إيحاشا و إضرار). This harm includes deceiving the buyer or seller and creating conflict.
The prohibition aims to preserve trust and social harmony in transactions.
4
Identify the Exception
If no agreement has been reached (i.e., the parties are still negotiating without inclination), then increasing the bid is permissible as 'bai' man yazid' (auction).
This exception distinguishes legitimate competitive bidding from prohibited najsh.
5
Extend to Marriage Proposals
The commentary notes the same prohibition applies to marriage proposals: one should not propose to a woman who has already accepted another's proposal.
This analogy shows the principle's broader application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَضْلُ فِيمَا يَكَرَهُ
قال ونهى رسول الله عن النجش وهو ان يزيد فى الثمن ولا يريد الشراء ليرغب غيره قال عليه السلام لا تناجشوا قال وعن السوم على سوم غيره قال لايستام الرجل على سوم اخيه ولا يخطب على خطبة اخيه ولان فی ذالک ایحاشا و اضرار او هذا اذا تراضى المتعاقدان على مبلغ ثمن فى المساومة اما اذا لم يركن احدهما الى الآخر فهو بيع من يزيد ولا باس به على ما نذكره وما ذكرناه محمل النهي في النكاح ايضا
Section on what is disliked (makruh). He said: The Messenger of Allah forbade najsh, which is to increase the price without intending to buy so that others will be tempted. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not practice najsh.' He said: And about bidding on another's negotiation: He said: 'A man should not bid on his brother's negotiation, nor propose on his brother's proposal.' And that is because there is estrangement and harm in that. This [dislike] applies when the two contracting parties have agreed on a sum in the negotiation; but if one of them is not inclined to the other, then it is a sale by auction (bai' man yazid) and there is no harm in it, as we will mention. And what we have mentioned also applies to the prohibition in marriage.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage from the commentary Ashraf ul-Hadaya addresses two related prohibitions in sales: najsh (artificial inflation) and bidding on another's ongoing negotiation (السوم على سوم الغير). The author begins by stating that the Prophet (PBUH) forbade najsh, defined as increasing the price of an item without any intention to purchase, solely to entice others to bid higher. The hadith 'Do not practice najsh' indicates a clear prohibition. Next, the commentary discusses the prohibition of bidding on a negotiation that has already been settled between two parties. The hadith states that one should not bid on his brother's negotiation, nor propose marriage to someone already proposed to. The reason given is that such actions cause estrangement (إيحاش) and harm (إضرار). However, the commentary clarifies that this ruling applies only after the two parties have mutually agreed on a price; if they are still in the initial negotiation without inclination, it is permissible to outbid, as in an auction (بَيْعُ مَنْ يَزِيدُ). The same principle applies to marriage proposals: after acceptance, further proposals are prohibited. This passage skillfully distinguishes between legitimate competitive bidding and deceitful inflation.

Key Terms
النَّجْش (an-najsh): Increasing the price of an item without intending to buy, only to entice others.
السّوْم على سوم الغير (as-saum 'ala saum al-ghair): Bidding on an item while another person has already negotiated a price with the seller.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes najsh from permissible auction bidding?
A) Najsh involves a third party, while auction is between two parties.
B) In najsh, the person increasing the price has no intention to buy, while in auction, all bidders intend to buy.
C) Najsh is prohibited only after the sale is finalized.
D) Auction bidding is always prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Najsh and overbidding on a settled negotiation are prohibited due to deceit and harm; auction is permissible when no prior agreement exists.

The Prohibition of Najash and Bidding Over Another's Bid
Explaining prohibition of najash and al-sum 'ala som gherih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prohibited najash and permissible auction, and apply the Hanafi ruling that such acts are makruh tahrimi without invalidating the sale.

Core Idea
Deception without intent to buy is makruh tahrimi, but the sale remains valid; auction is permissible.

In this lesson, we examine two related transactions that the Prophet expressly forbade: najash (artificial inflation) and bidding over a brother's bid. The Hanafi school classifies these as makruh tahrimi when they involve deception or harm, but the sale itself is not invalid. Understanding the conditions that trigger prohibition versus permissibility is essential for distinguishing between forbidden manipulation and lawful auction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited acts and their definitions
From the passage, identify najash (increasing price without intent to buy) and al-sum 'ala som gherih (bidding over an already agreed price). Note that the hadith provides direct prohibition.
Najash is specific to deception; sum 'ala som gherih covers both undercutting and overbidding.
2
Understand the distinction between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi
The introduction explains that if the defect is incidental (amr mujawir), the sale is makruh, not fasid. Within karahah, tahrimi is closer to haram, tanzihi closer to mubah. Here, the ruling is makruh tahrimi due to deception and harm.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi usul and affects the gravity of the prohibition.
3
Recognize the condition that triggers the prohibition
The prohibition applies only when the two contracting parties have already agreed on a price. If no agreement is reached, the third person's bid is not prohibited but is considered a permissible auction (bai' min yazid).
This condition is derived from the hadith's context and the illa of causing alienation and harm.
4
Apply the ruling to auction and marriage proposals
The passage extends the same principle to marriage: a man may not propose if the woman's heart has inclined to another suitor. If no inclination, it is permissible. Auction is cited as a valid practice based on the Prophet's own action.
The same underlying cause of harm determines the ruling in both contexts.

اور ایک آدمی کے معاملہ چکانے پر بھاؤ کرنے سے بھی منع فرمایا ہے چنانچہ حدیث ہے لا یستـام الـرجل علی سوم اخيه ولا يخـطـب على خطبة اخيه ۔ یعنی کوئی آدمی اپنے بھائی کے چکانے پر بھاؤ نہ کرے اور اپنے بھائی کی منگنی پرمنگنی نہ کرے۔ لا يستام الرجل علی سوم اخیر کی صورت یہ ہے کہ دو آدمی ایک سامان کے ثمن پر راضی ہو گئے یعنی بائع بیچنے پر راضی ہو گیا اور مشتری خریدنے پر راضی ہو گیا۔ اب تیسرا آدمی آ کر کہتا ہے کہ میں اسی سامان کو اس ثمن سے کم کے عوض دیدوں گا ظاہر ہے اس صورت میں سامان والے کا نقصان ہے اور اگر اس نے سامان والے سے کہا کہ میں یہ سامان زائد ثمن کے عوض خرید لوں گا تو اس صورت میں مشتری کا نقصان ہے پس سوم علی سوم غیرہ کی صورت میں احد المتعاقدین کے قلب میں وحشت ڈالنا ہے اور اس کو ضرر پہنچانا ہے اور یہ دونوں چیزیں قبیح ہیں مگر بیع سے جدا بھی ہو جاتی ہیں اس لئے ان امور قبیحہ کی وجہ سے بیع مکر وہ ہوگی۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سوم علی سوم غیرہ اسی وقت مکروہ ہے جبکہ عاقدین معاملہ چکانے میں کسی قدرشمن پر راضی ہو گئے ہوں اور اگر ابھی تک کوئی کسی کی طرف مائل نہیں ہوا اور تیسرے آدمی نے آکر پیسے بڑھا دیئے تو یہ سوم علی سوم غیرہ نہ ہوگا بلکہ یہ بیع من یزید ہے یعنی نیلامی کر کے اور بولی بول کر بیچنا ہے اور نیلامی کر کے بیچنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے جیسا کہ حضرت انس کی حدیث ہے ان النبی صلی الله عليه وسلم باع قدحاً وحَلْساً بيع من یزید یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ایک پیالہ اور ایک ٹاٹ بیع من یزید کے طور پر بیچا ہے یعنی نیلام کر کے بیچا۔ اور نکاح میں حدیث لا يخطب على خطبة اخيه كامل بھی یہی ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے یعنی اگر عورت کا قلب پیغام نکاح دینے والے کی طرف مائل ہو گیا تو اب دوسرے آدمی کے لئے اس عورت کو پیغام نکاح دینا مکروہ ہے اور اگر عورت کا قلب مائل نہیں ہوا تو پھر اس کو پیغام نکاح دینے میں کوئی کراہت نہیں ہے۔
Section on what is disliked. Translation: Chapter on the disliked aspects of sale. Book of Sales. Commentary: Karahah (dislike) is lower in rank than fasid (invalid), but it is a part of it, therefore he (al-Quduri) delayed the types of sale from fasid sale. It is mentioned in books of Usul al-Fiqh that if the defect is due to an incidental matter, it is makruh, and if due to an inseparable attribute, it is fasid. Karahah is of two types: makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi. Makruh tahrimi is closer to haram, and makruh tanzihi is closer to mubah. Legal status and definition of najash. He said: The Messenger of Allah forbade najash, which is to increase the price without intending to buy in order to entice others. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not practice najash.' He said: And (he forbade) bidding over the bid of another. He said: 'A man should not bid over the bid of his brother, nor propose over the proposal of his brother.' Because in that there is causing alienation and harm. This is when the two contracting parties have agreed on a certain price in the negotiation. But if one of them has not inclined to the other, then it is a sale by bidding (auction) and there is no harm in it, as we will mention. And what we have mentioned also applies to the prohibition in marriage. Translation: Quduri said: The Prophet forbade najash. Najash is to increase the price while not intending to buy, so that others are enticed. The Prophet said: 'Do not practice najash.' Quduri said: And do not bid over the bid of another. The Prophet said: 'A man should not bid over the bid of his brother, nor propose over the proposal of his brother.' Because doing so causes alienation and harm to the other. This dislike is when the contracting parties have agreed on a certain amount of price in the negotiation. However, if neither of them is inclined to the other, then it is a sale by auction and there is no harm in it, as we will mention. And the same applies to marriage as we have mentioned. Commentary: Najash (with fatha on nun and jim) – the Prophet forbade the sale of najash. The sale of najash is when the buyer has set the price equal to the value, but another person increases the price, saying: I will take it for this much more than the price stated by the buyer, while he does not intend to buy. His sole purpose is to deceive the buyer and entice him so that the buyer increases his offer. Deception is a bad thing that is incidental to this sale, and due to the bad thing being incidental, the sale becomes makruh. Therefore this sale is makruh. And the Prophet's saying is 'Do not practice najash', i.e., do not commit the sale of najash. However, if the buyer has not set a price equal to the value, and another person increases the price slightly to make it equal to the value, while he does not intend to buy, then this is permissible because it benefits the seller (a Muslim) without harming the buyer. And it is obvious that there is no harm in this. And he also forbade bidding over a man's transaction. Thus the hadith: 'A man should not bid over the bid of his brother, nor propose over the proposal of his brother.' That is, no man should bid over the bid of his brother, nor propose over the proposal of his brother. The situation of 'bidding over the bid of his brother' is that two men have agreed on the price of a commodity, i.e., the seller agreed to sell and the buyer agreed to buy. Now a third person comes and says: I will give this commodity for less than this price. Obviously in this case the seller suffers loss. And if he said to the seller: I will buy this commodity for a higher price, then in this case the buyer suffers loss. So in the case of bidding over another's bid, there is causing alienation in the heart of one of the two contracting parties and causing him harm. Both of these things are bad (qabih). They are separate from the sale, so due to these bad things, the sale becomes makruh. The author of Hidayah says: Bidding over another's bid is disliked only when the two parties have agreed on a certain price in the transaction. If neither is inclined to the other yet, and a third person comes and increases the price, then this is not bidding over another's bid, but rather it is a sale by auction (bai' min yazid), i.e., selling by auction and bidding. There is no harm in selling by auction, as in the hadith of Anas: The Prophet sold a cup and a mat by auction, i.e., he sold them by auction. And the same applies to marriage regarding the hadith 'Do not propose over the proposal of his brother', i.e., if the woman's heart has inclined towards the one who proposed, then it is makruh for another man to propose to her. But if her heart has not inclined, then there is no dislike in proposing to her.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the chapter of disliked sales from Al-Hidayah. It begins by explaining the general ruling on makruh (disliked) transactions, distinguishing between makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked, close to haram) and makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked, close to mubah). The main focus is on two prohibited practices: najash (artificial price inflation) and al-sum 'ala som gherih (bidding over another's bid). The author presents the hadith proofs: the Prophet explicitly forbade najash, which is defined as increasing the price without intending to buy, simply to lure others. The same hadith also forbids bidding over one's brother's bid and proposing over his proposal. The commentator explains that the prohibition applies only when the parties have reached some agreement in negotiation; if no one has yet inclined to the other, then it becomes a permissible auction (bai' min yazid). He cites the example of the Prophet himself selling by auction. The same principle applies to marriage proposals: if the woman has inclined to a previous suitor, another man may not propose, but if she has not, it is permissible. The passage thus clarifies the conditions that make these acts disliked versus permissible, emphasizing the underlying reasons of causing alienation (iḥāshā) and harm (ḍarar).

Key Terms
نجش (najash): Increasing the price of an item without intending to buy, solely to entice others to buy at a higher price.
سوم على سوم غيره (al-sum 'ala som gherih): Bidding over a bid that has already been agreed upon between buyer and seller, either by offering a lower price (harming seller) or higher price (harming buyer).
بيـع من يزيد (bai' min yazid): Sale by auction where multiple buyers bid openly and the highest bidder wins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is bidding over another's bid (al-sum 'ala som gherih) considered makruh tahrimi?
A) Whenever a third person offers a higher price than the current bidder.
B) Only when the two contracting parties have already agreed on a price.
C) Only when the third person offers a lower price than the agreed amount.
D) In all cases, regardless of prior agreement.

Key Takeaway
Najash and bidding over another's bid are makruh tahrimi due to deception and harm, but the sale remains valid; auction is permissible when no prior agreement exists.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
8 min
Buying Over Another's Offer (Sum 'ala Sum Ghayrihi)
Explains the ruling and conditions of third-party intervention after agreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of sum 'ala sum ghayrihi, identify the condition that triggers the ruling, and distinguish it from permissible auction.

Core Idea
Intervening after mutual agreement causes harm and is makruh; before agreement it is permissible auction.

This lesson examines a common market practice where a third person makes a better offer after two parties have already agreed on a price and terms. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between harmful interference (makruh) and legitimate competitive bidding (permissible). Understanding this distinction protects the integrity of contracts and prevents unjust harm to one of the contracting parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the exact act being discussed: sum 'ala sum ghayrihi (buying over another's offer). The ruling is makruh (disliked) because it involves causing harm to one of the original parties.
The sale itself is not invalid; it is simply disliked due to the means.
2
Locate the key condition
The prohibition applies only after the two parties have mutually agreed on a price and have become inclined to conclude the transaction. If no such agreement exists, the intervention is not sum 'ala sum ghayrihi.
This condition is the crux: without agreement, it becomes bay' min yazid (auction) which is permissible.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith of Anas (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) sold a cup and a mat by auction (bay' min yazid). This establishes the permissibility of auction, which is the exception to the general prohibition.
The hadith is ahad (single narration) but sufficient to establish the rule.
4
Apply the analogy to marriage proposals
The same principle applies to marriage: if a woman's heart has inclined to a suitor, another man proposing to her is makruh; if not, it is permissible. This shows consistency across transactions.
The hadith 'Do not propose over the proposal of your brother' supports this analogy.
5
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah)
The practical difference is that the sale in sum 'ala sum ghayrihi is valid but makruh, while in auction it is completely permissible and encouraged for fair pricing.
This distinction helps in real-world transactions like eBay bids vs. private deals.

الرجل علی سوم اخیر کی صورت یہ ہے کہ دو آدمی ایک سامان کے شمن پر راضی ہو گئے یعنی بائے بیچنے پر راضی ہو گیا اور مشتری خرید نے پر راضی ہو گیا۔ اب تیسرا آدمی آ کر کہتا ہے کہ میں اسی سامان کو اس شمن سے کم کے عوض دیدوں گا ظاہر ہے اس صورت میں سامان والے کا نقصان ہے اور اگر اس نے سامان والے سے کہا کہ میں یہ سامان زائد شمن کے عوض خرید لوں گا تو اس صورت میں مشتری کا نقصان ہے پس سوم علی سوم غیرہ کی صورت میں احد المتعاقدین کے قلب میں وحشت ڈالنا ہے اور اس کو ضرر پہنچانا ہے اور یہ دونوں چیزیں قبیح ہیں مگر بیچ سے جدا بھی ہو جاتی ہیں اس لئے ان امور قبیحہ کی وجہ سے بیع مکر وہ ہوگی۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سوم علی سوم غیرہ اسی وقت مکروہ ہے جبکہ عاقدین معاملہ چکانے میں کسی قدرشن پر راضی ہو گئے ہوں اور اگر ابھی تک کوئی کسی کی طرف مائل نہیں ہوا اور تیسرے آدمی نے آکر پیسے بڑھا دیئے تو یہ سوم علی سوم غیرہ نہ ہوگا بلکہ یہ بیچ من یزید ہے یعنی نیلامی کر کے اور بولی بول کر بیچنا ہے اور نیلامی کر کے بیچنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے جیسا کہ حضرت انس کی حدیث ہے ان النبی صلی الله عليه وسلم باع قدحاً وحَلْساً بيع من یزید یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ایک پیالہ اور ایک ٹاٹ بیع من یزید کے طور پر بیچا ہے یعنی نیلام کر کے بیچا۔ اور نکاح میں حدیث لا يخطب على خطبة اخيه كامل بھی یہی ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے یعنی اگر عورت کا قلب پیغام نکاح دینے والے کی طرف مائل ہو گیا تو اب دوسرے آدمی کے لئے اس عورت کو پیغام نکاح دینا مکروہ ہے اور اگر عورت کا قلب مائل نہیں ہوا تو پھر اس کو پیغام نکاح دینے میں کوئی کراہت نہیں ہے۔
The condition of the third party over the offer of another is that two people have agreed on a price of a commodity, meaning the seller agreed to sell and the buyer agreed to buy. Then a third person comes and says that I will give this same commodity for less than that price. Obviously in this case there is loss to the seller. And if he said to the seller that I will buy this commodity for a higher price, then in that case there is loss to the buyer. So in the case of sum 'ala sum ghayrihi, there is casting unrest into the heart of one of the two contractors and causing him harm. Both these things are reprehensible, but they are separate from the sale, therefore due to these reprehensible matters the sale becomes makruh. The author of al-Hidayah says that sum 'ala sum ghayrihi is makruh only when the parties have agreed upon some measure of settling the transaction. And if no one has yet inclined to the other and a third person came and increased the price, then this is not sum 'ala sum ghayrihi; rather this is bay' min yazid, meaning selling by auction and bidding. And there is no harm in selling by auction, as in the hadith of Anas (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) sold a cup and a mat by bay' min yazid, i.e., sold by auction. And in marriage, the hadith 'Do not propose over the proposal of your brother' is also the same as what we have mentioned, meaning if the woman's heart has inclined towards the one giving the marriage proposal, then for another man it is makruh to propose to that woman, and if the woman's heart has not inclined, then there is no dislike in proposing to her.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage from the commentary of Al-Hidayah explains the ruling of sum 'ala sum ghayrihi (buying over another's offer). It is a transaction where two parties have already agreed on a price, and a third person intervenes by offering better terms to one side, causing loss to the other. This is considered makruh (disliked) because it causes harm and sows discord. However, if no agreement has been reached yet, a third person making a better offer is not prohibited; it is considered bay' min yazid (auction), which is permissible based on the hadith of Anas (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) sold by auction. The same principle applies to marriage proposals: after the woman's inclination is known, another proposal is makruh; before inclination, it is permissible. The key condition is that the prohibition applies only after the parties have mutually agreed; before that, intervention is allowed.

Key Terms
سوم علی سوم غیرہ (sum 'ala sum ghayrihi): A transaction where a third person makes a better offer to one party after the two original parties have already agreed on a price, causing loss to the other party.
بیع من یزید (bay' min yazid): Sale by auction where items are sold to the highest bidder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which situation is sum 'ala sum ghayrihi considered makruh according to the Hanafi school?
A) When a third person offers a higher price to the seller before any agreement
B) When a third person offers a lower price to the seller after the buyer and seller have agreed on a price
C) When a third person offers a higher price to the buyer after agreement
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Sum 'ala sum ghayrihi is makruh only after mutual agreement; before agreement it is permissible auction.

The Ruling on Meeting Caravans (Talaqqi al-Jalb) and Its Scenarios
Explains the prohibition and its conditions with four scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talaqqi al-jalb and apply the four scenarios to determine whether a sale is makruh or permissible.

Core Idea
Talaqqi al-jalb is makruh only when it causes harm or deception; otherwise it is permissible.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on meeting caravans before they reach the market. The passage from Al-Hidayah explains that the prohibition is conditional upon harm to townspeople or concealment of prices. Through four concrete scenarios, we will see how the ruling changes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is talaqqi al-jalb (going out to meet incoming caravans to buy goods before they reach the market). The Prophet (SAW) prohibited it, but the prohibition is not absolute.
The hadith is cited: 'He forbade meeting caravans.'
2
Determine the condition for prohibition
The prohibition applies when it causes harm (ضَرَر) to the townspeople. If there is no harm, it is permissible.
Harm includes causing price inflation or depriving locals of goods.
3
Identify the exception for price concealment
Even if no direct harm, if the buyer conceals the city price from the caravan sellers, the act becomes makruh due to deception (غَرُور).
Deception is a separate ground for dislike.
4
Apply to the four scenarios
Scenarios: (1) famine + buying all stock, (2) no shortage, (3) cheap purchase + concealed price, (4) cheap purchase + no concealment. Only scenarios (1) and (3) are makruh.
Scenario (1) causes harm; (3) involves deception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلقی جلب جبکہ اہل بلد کو نقصان ہوتا ہو مکروہ ہے
قال وعن تلقى الجلب وهذا اذا كان يضربا هل البلد فان كان لايضر فلا باس به الااذا لبس السعر على الواردين فحينئذ يكره لما فيه من الغرور والضرر
ترجمہ قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے تلقی جلب سے منع فرمایا ہے اور یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ اہل شہر کو ضرر پہنچے پس اگر اہل شہر کو ضرر نہ پہنچے تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے مگر جبکہ آنے والوں پر بھاؤ چھپا دیا تو اس وقت مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اس میں دھوکہ اور ضرر ہے۔
تشریح تلقی جلب کی چند صورتیں ہیں۔
ا یہ کہ شہر میں قحط ہے لیکن جب شہر کے بعض تاجروں کو غلہ کے قافلہ کی آمد کی اطلاع ملی تو انھوں نے شہر سے باہر نکل کر قافلہ والوں سے سارا غلہ خرید لیا تا کہ حسب منشاء قیمت پر فروخت کریں۔
یہ کہ شہر میں غلہ کی کمی نہ ہو۔ اور کچھ تاجروں نے شہر سے باہر نکل کر قافلہ کا سارا غلہ خرید لیا ہو۔
(۳) یہ کہ قافلہ والوں سے سستے داموں غلہ خرید لیا اور شہر کا بھاؤ ان پر خفی رکھا اور وہ خود بھی شہر کے بھاؤ سے ناواقف ہوں۔ یہ کہ قافلہ والوں سے غلہ تو ستا ہی خرید انگر ان پر بھی بھاؤ مخفی نہیں رکھا۔ ان میں پہلی اور تیسری صورت مکروہ ہے۔ پہلی تو اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں شہر کے لوگ قحط اور غلہ نہ ہونے سے ضرر اور پریشانی میں مبتلا ہیں اور تاجروں کے اس عمل سے شہر کے لوگوں کی پریشانی میں مزید اضافہ ہوگا اورکسی کو پریشانی میں مبتلا کرنا امریح ہے مگر یہ امرفتیح ایسا ہے جو بیچ سے جدا ہو سکتا ہے اس لئے اس کی وجہ سے بیچ مکر وہ ہوگی ۔ اور تیسری صورت میں چونکہ آنے والے قافلہ کے لوگوں پر بھاؤ چھپا کر چونکہ ان کو دھوکہ دیا گیا ہے اور دھو کہ دینا امر قبیح ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی بیچ مکروہ ہوگی اور باقی دو صورتوں میں چونکہ یہ خرابیاں نہیں ہیں اس لئے ان میں بیچ بالا کراہت درست ہوگی ۔
Talaqqi al-jalb: when it causes harm to the townspeople, it is makruh. He said: 'And about meeting caravans.' And this is when it harms the townspeople. If it does not harm, then there is no harm in it, except when they conceal the price from the arrivals; then at that time it is makruh because of the deception and harm. Translation: Quduri says that the Prophet (SAW) forbade meeting caravans. And this ruling is when it causes harm to the townspeople. So if it does not cause harm, then there is no issue, except when they conceal the price from the arrivals; then at that time it is makruh because of deception and harm. Explanation: There are several scenarios of talaqqi al-jalb. (1) There is a famine in the city, but when some merchants get news of a grain caravan arriving, they go out of the city and buy all the grain from the caravan to sell at a price they desire. (2) There is no shortage of grain in the city, and some merchants go out and buy all the grain from the caravan. (3) They buy grain cheap from the caravan and conceal the city price from them while they themselves are unaware of the city price. (4) They buy grain cheap from the caravan but do not conceal the price. Among these, the first and third scenarios are makruh. The first because in this case the city people are suffering from famine and lack of grain, and the merchants' action increases their distress, and causing distress to someone is a reprehensible act; but this act is separate from the sale, so the sale becomes makruh. And the third scenario because the caravan people are deceived by concealing the price, and deception is a reprehensible act, so the sale is makruh. In the other two scenarios, since these defects are not present, the sale is valid without dislike.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule of talaqqi al-jalb (meeting caravans) to intercept goods before they reach the market. Based on a hadith prohibition, it is makruh when it harms the townspeople. The commentator then lists four scenarios: (1) famine, (2) no shortage, (3) with deception, (4) without deception. Only the first (famine) and third (deception) are makruh because of harm or deceit. The second (no shortage) and fourth (no deception) are permissible. The key is that the prohibition is tied to harm or fraud.

Key Terms
تلقی جلب (talaqqi al-jalb): The act of going out to meet incoming caravans to buy goods before they reach the market, often to resell at a higher price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which of the following scenarios is talaqqi al-jalb considered makruh?
A) When merchants buy all the grain from a caravan during a famine.
B) When merchants buy all the grain from a caravan in normal conditions, concealing the city price.
C) When merchants buy grain from a caravan without concealing the price, during normal supply.
D) A and B are both makruh.

Key Takeaway
Talaqqi al-jalb is not inherently prohibited; it becomes makruh only when it involves harm to the public or deception of the seller.

Bay' al-Hadir li'l-Badi: Townsman Selling for a Villager
Explains the prohibition with two interpretations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two interpretations of the hadith 'لا يبيع حاضر لباد' and identify when the sale is makruh according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A townsman selling for a villager is makruh only when it causes harm to the townspeople.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on bay' al-hadir li'l-badi, derived from a prophetic hadith. The passage explains two interpretations: one where the townsman sells his own goods to villagers, and another where he acts as an agent for a villager. Both are considered makruh if they harm the townspeople or exploit the villager's ignorance. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the underlying cause of harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its prohibition
Locate the hadith 'لا يبيع حاضر لباد' in the passage. Recognize that it is a command (imperative) indicating prohibition. Note that the Hanafi school does not treat it as absolute.
The hadith is a primary evidence (dalil naqli) for this ruling.
2
Analyze the first interpretation
In the first interpretation, the 'lam' in 'li'l-badi' means 'from' (min). The townsman sells his own goods to the villager rather than to his fellow townspeople, seeking a higher price. This harms the townspeople, especially in times of scarcity.
Two sub-scenarios: townspeople in abundance (no harm) vs. in famine (harm).
3
Analyze the second interpretation
In the second interpretation, the 'lam' retains its original meaning of 'for'. The townsman acts as an agent (wakeel) for the villager, selling the villager's goods at a high price because the villager is unaware of market prices. This harms both the townspeople (who pay more) and potentially the villager (if deceived).
The hadith 'Leave the people; Allah provides for some through others' supports this.
4
Determine the condition for makruh
The ruling of makruh hinges on the presence of harm (darar). If no harm occurs (e.g., townspeople are not in need, or the villager is not exploited), the sale is permissible. The passage explicitly states: 'if it is not like that, there is no harm due to absence of harm.'
This shows that the prohibition is not absolute but conditional.
5
Apply the condition to hypotheticals
Practice applying the ruling: In a scenario where a townsman sells grain to a villager during a famine, it is makruh. If the townspeople have abundant supplies, it is permissible. Similarly, acting as an agent for a villager is makruh only if it causes harm or deception.
The underlying principle is preventing harm to the community and exploitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دیہاتی کے لئے شہری کے بیچنے کا حکم
قال وعن بيع الحاظر للبادى فقد قال لا يبيع الحافر للبادى وهذا اذا كان اهل البلدة في قحط وعوزو هو يبيع من اهل البلد و طمعا فى الثمن الغالي لما فيه من الاضرار بهم اما اذا لم يكن كذالك لا باس به لا نعدام الضرر
ترجمہ اور دیہاتی کے لئے شہری کے بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے چنانچہ رسول اللہ علیہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے شہری دیہاتی کے واسطے فروخت نہ کرے اور یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ اہل شہر قحط اور محتاجی میں ہوں اور شہری آدمی دیہاتی سے اس لالچ میں فروخت کرتا ہے کہ اس کو گراں قیمت حاصل ہوگی کیونکہ اس میں اہل شہر کا ضرر ہے بہر حال جب ایسا نہ ہو تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں کیونکہ (اب) ضر ر نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہے کہ بیج الحاضر للہادی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ لا يبع الحاضر للبادی۔ حدیث اور متن کے اس جملہ کی دو طرح تشریح ہو سکتی ہیں۔
پہلی تشریح ایک تو یہ کہ لبادی میں لام من کے معنی میں ہو اس صورت میں مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ کسی شہری کے پاس غلہ ہے لیکن وہ شہر والوں کے ہاتھ فروخت نہیں کرتا بلکہ بادیہ نشیں اور دیہاتیوں کے ہاتھ فروخت کرتا ہے اور اس سے مقصد گراں قیمت وصول کرنا ہے کیونکہ شہر کے لوگ بھاؤ اور معاملات سے واقف ہونے کی بناء پر گراں قیمت پر خریدنے کے لئے آمادہ نہ ہوں گے ۔ اور گاؤں کے لوگ اپنی سادگی کی وجہ سے اس کے چکر میں آجائیں گے پس اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں شہر کے لوگ یا تو وسعت میں ہوں گے اور ان کو اس عمل سے یعنی گاؤں والوں کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنے سے کوئی ضرر نہ ہوگا اور یا شہر کے لوگ قحط اور تنگی میں ہوں گے اور اس کے عمل سے باشندگان شہر کو تکلیف ہوگی پس اگر دوسری صورت ہے تو بیع مکروہ ہے اور اگر پہلی صورت ہے تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ دوسری تشریح یہ ہے کہ للبادی کالام اپنی اصل پر ہو اس صورت میں مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ شہری دیہاتی کا وکیل بن کر اس کی طرف سے فروخت نہ کرے اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک دیہاتی باہر سے غلہ لے کر شہر میں آیا پس ایک شہری نے اس سے کہا کہ تو شہریوں کی عادتوں اور معاملات سے واقف نہیں ہے اس لئے تو مت بیچ میں ان سے زیادہ واقف ہوں پس یہ شہری گاؤں والے کا وکیل بن کر گراں قیمت پر اس کا غلہ فروخت کرتا ہے تو یہ بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ صورت بھی لوگوں کے لئے ضرر رساں ہے اس لئے کہ دیہاتی اگر بذات خود فروخت کرتا تو اپنے حساب سے بیچتا اور ستا بیچتا چنانچہ رسول اللہ کا قول ہے دعوا الناس يرزق الله بعضهم من بعض یعنی لوگوں کو چھوڑ دو اللہ تعالیٰ بعض کو بعض سے رزق دیتا ہے یعنی انکو خود کاروبار کرنے دو اس لئے کہ ایک انسان دوسرے انسان کی روزی کا ذریعہ ہوتا ہے۔
Ruling of a townsman selling for a villager. He said: 'And about the sale of the townsman for the villager, for he said: The townsman should not sell for the villager.' And this is when the townspeople are in famine and need, and he sells to the townspeople out of greed for a high price, because it harms them. But if it is not like that, there is no harm due to absence of harm. Translation: And it is forbidden for a townsman to sell for a villager. Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (SAW) said: 'The townsman should not sell for the villager.' And this ruling is when the townspeople are in famine and need, and the townsman sells to the villager out of greed to get a high price, because it harms the townspeople. In any case, when it is not so, there is no harm because there is no harm. Explanation: Quduri says that bay' al-hadir li'l-badi is makruh because the Prophet said: 'The townsman should not sell for the villager.' There are two interpretations of this hadith. First interpretation: لام in للبادی means 'from' (من), meaning that a townsman has grain but does not sell it to the townspeople; instead he sells it to the villagers, seeking a high price, because the townspeople, being aware of prices, will not pay high, while villagers in their simplicity will fall into his trap. This has two sub-scenarios: either the townspeople are in abundance (no harm) or in famine (harm). If harm, the sale is makruh; if not, no issue. Second interpretation: لام remains in its original meaning (للام), meaning that a townsman should not act as an agent for a villager. The scenario: a villager brings grain to the city, and a townsman says: 'You are not familiar with the city's customs, so don't sell; I will sell for you.' The townsman then sells the grain at a high price. This is also makruh because it harms the townspeople, as the villager would have sold cheaply. The Prophet said: 'Leave the people; Allah provides for some through others.'
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage deals with the prohibition of a townsman selling for a villager, derived from the hadith 'لا يبيع حاضر لباد'. Two interpretations are given: (1) the townsman sells his own goods to the villagers rather than the townspeople, harming the townspeople in times of need; (2) the townsman acts as an agent for the villager, selling at a high price and depriving the townspeople of cheap goods. Both are makruh when they cause harm. The underlying principle is preventing harm to the community and exploitation of the villager's ignorance.

Key Terms
بیع الحاضر للبادی (bay' al-hadir li'l-badi): A townsman selling goods to a villager or acting as his agent, causing harm to the townspeople.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first interpretation of the hadith, what causes the sale to be makruh?
A) The townsman sells to a villager
B) The townsman sells at a high price
C) The townsman sells his goods to a villager when townspeople are in need
D) The townsman acts as an agent

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on bay' al-hadir li'l-badi depends on the presence of harm; the sale is only makruh when it harms the townspeople or exploits the villager.

The Ruling on a Townsman Selling for a Villager (بيع الحاضر للبادي)
Explains the prohibition and conditions of a townsman selling for a villager.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bai' al-hadir lil-badi and identify the condition under which it becomes makruh.

Core Idea
A townsman selling for a villager is makruh only when it harms the townspeople; otherwise it is permissible.

This lesson examines the classical Hanafi ruling on a townsman selling for a villager, based on the hadith 'la yabi' hadir li badin.' The commentator al-Quduri clarifies that the prohibition is not absolute; it depends on the presence of harm. We will analyze the hadith, the two interpretations, and the legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal classification according to the Hanafi school: bai' al-hadir lil-badi is makruh tanzih.
The act is the townsman selling for the villager, either by selling his own goods to the villager or by acting as the villager's agent.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith 'لا يبع حاضر لباد' (The townsman should not sell for the villager). Identify its transmission and authority.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), which affects the level of obligation.
3
Understand the two interpretations
The commentator provides two interpretations: (1) 'lilbadi' with lam meaning 'min' – the townsman sells his own goods to villagers; (2) lam on its original meaning – the townsman acts as agent for the villager.
Both interpretations share the condition of harm to townspeople.
4
Apply the condition of harm
The ruling of karahah applies only when the townspeople are in need and the townsman's action causes them harm. If no harm, the sale is permissible.
Harm is the key factor; the sale itself is valid and not defective.
5
Note the Hanafi position
The relied-upon position is that the sale is makruh tanzih when harm is present, and mubah otherwise. This differs from some other schools that consider it haram absolutely.
The karahah is due to external harm, not a defect in the contract.

He said: And regarding the sale of the townsman for the villager, he (the Prophet) said: 'The townsman should not sell for the villager.' And this is when the people of the town are in drought and need, and he sells from the people of the town, desiring a high price because of the harm to them. But if it is not like that, there is no harm because of the absence of harm. [Urdu: He forbade the townsman selling for the villager. Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The townsman should not sell for the villager. This ruling is when the townspeople are in drought and need, and the townsman sells to the villager out of greed to get a high price, because in that there is harm to the townspeople. However, when it is not like that, there is no harm because now there is no harm. Commentary: Al-Quduri says that the sale of the townsman for the villager is makruh because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The townsman should not sell for the villager.' There are two interpretations of this hadith and the text. First interpretation: The 'lam' in 'lilbadi' is in the meaning of 'min' (from). In this case, the meaning is that a townsman has grain but does not sell it to the townspeople; rather, he sells it to the desert-dwellers villagers, aiming to get a high price because the townspeople, being aware of prices and transactions, will not agree to buy at a high price, while the villagers, due to their simplicity, will fall into his trap. So there are two scenarios: either the townspeople are in abundance and suffer no harm from this action (selling to villagers), or the townspeople are in drought and hardship and suffer harm from his action. If the second scenario, the sale is makruh; if the first, there is no harm. Second interpretation: The 'lam' is on its original meaning (for). In this case, the meaning is that the townsman should not act as an agent for the villager and sell on his behalf. The scenario: A villager brings grain from outside into the city. A townsman tells him: 'You are not familiar with the habits and dealings of the townspeople, so do not sell; I am more familiar.' Then this townsman becomes the villager's agent and sells his grain at a high price. This is also makruh because this scenario also harms people, because if the villager sold himself, he would sell at a reasonable price. Indeed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Leave the people; Allah provides for some through others' — meaning let them do business themselves, because one person is a means of provision for another.]
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar on the prohibition of a townsman selling for a villager. The commentator explains that the hadith 'la yabi' hadir li badin' is the proof. Two interpretations are given: (1) The townsman sells his own goods to villagers instead of townspeople, harming the townspeople when they are in need. (2) The townsman acts as an agent for the villager, selling the villager's goods at a high price, thus depriving the townspeople of affordable goods and the villager of fair pricing. In both cases, the sale is makruh when it causes harm; if no harm, it is permissible. This ruling is based on the principle of preventing harm (darar) and following the prophetic command. The commentator emphasizes that the karahah is due to external harm, not defect in the contract itself, so the sale is valid but disliked.

Key Terms
بيع الحاضر للبادي (bai' al-hadir lil-badi): A townsman selling for a villager, either by selling his own goods to the villager instead of townspeople, or by acting as an agent for the villager.
كراهة (karahah): Disliked but not prohibited; the sale is valid but blameworthy due to external harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling ties the prohibition to harm; the sale is makruh only when it causes harm to townspeople, not in all cases.

Karahah Does Not Invalidate the Sale
Ruling statement: karahah does not invalidate sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that external defects cause karahah not fasad, and identify the distinction between defects in the contract's substance/conditions vs. external defects.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a sale is still valid if its defect is external to the contract's core and conditions; the flaw only makes it makruh.

This passage concludes a series of rules about disliked sales. Al-Quduri here establishes a critical principle: that karahah (dislike) does not equal invalidity (fasad). The key is where the defect lies — if it is external to the contract's substance (sulb al-aqd) and conditions (shurut al-sihhah), the sale remains valid but is disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching ruling
The passage states that all the previously mentioned sales are makruh, but they are NOT fasid (invalid). Focus on the negative: 'wa la yufsid bihi al-bay' (the sale is not invalidated by it).
This is a general ruling covering multiple cases from earlier sections.
2
Locate the talil (legal reasoning)
The reasoning is given immediately after the ruling: 'al-fasad fi ma'na kharij za'id, la fi sulb al-aqd wa la fi shurut al-sihhah.' (fasad is in an external additional meaning, not in the substance of the contract nor in the conditions of validity).
This is a causal explanation (talil) that differentiates between internal and external defects.
3
Deconstruct the key terms
Understand three essential terms: sulb al-aqd (the core of the contract, i.e., ijab and qabul), shurut al-sihhah (conditions of validity like ownership and capacity), and ma'na kharij (an external meaning that is adjacent but not integral).
These terms are fundamental to Hanafi contract theory.
4
Apply the principle to a specific case
Consider the sale of a commodity during Friday prayer. The defect (missing obligatory prayer) is external; the offer, acceptance, ownership, and all core conditions are sound. Therefore, the sale is valid but makruh.
The external defect does not affect the contract's essential elements.
5
Distinguish from fasad
Contrast with a fasid sale, e.g., selling a stolen item. Here the defect is internal: the condition of seller ownership is missing, so the contract is fasid. The distinction lies in whether the defect touches the core or conditions.
Not all defects are equal; the location of the defect determines the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال كل ذالك يكره لما ذكرنا ولا يفسد به البيع لان الفساد في معنى خارج زائد لا في صلب العقد ولا في شرائط الصحة. اور یہ سب بیوع مکروہ ہیں اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے اور کراہت کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ فسادا ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے ہے جو خارج سے زائد ہے صاب عقد میں نہیں ہے اور نہ شرائ کا صحت میں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اول فصل سے لے کر اب تک جتنی بیوع مذکور ہوئیں سب مکروہ ہیں اور کراہت کی وجہ سے بیچ فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ فساد یعنی فتح ایسے معنی میں ہے جو عقد سے خارج ہے البتہ عقد کے مجاور ہے صلب عقد اور شر انکا صحت میں کوئی قباحت نہیں ہے اور جو قباحت معنی خارج مجاور میں ہوتی ہے اس کی وجہ سے بیع مکروہ ہوتی ہے فاسد نہیں ہوتی اس لئے مذکورہ تمام صورتوں میں مگر وہ ہو گی فاسد نہ ہوگی۔
He said: All that is makruh for what we have mentioned, and the sale is not invalidated by it, because corruption (fasad) is in an external added meaning, not in the substance of the contract nor in the conditions of validity. [Urdu: And all these sales are makruh due to the proof we have mentioned, and due to karahah the sale will not become fasid (invalid), because fasad is due to a meaning that is external and additional; it is not in the substance of the contract nor in the conditions of validity. Commentary: Al-Quduri says that from the first chapter until now, all the sales mentioned are makruh, and due to karahah the sale will not become fasid, because fasad is due to a meaning external to the contract, merely adjacent to it; there is no defect in the substance of the contract nor in the conditions of validity. And the defect that occurs in an external adjacent meaning causes the sale to be makruh, not fasid. Therefore, in all mentioned cases, it will be makruh, not fasid.]
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This is a general ruling summarizing the legal effect of the previously mentioned makruh sales. The commentator clarifies that although these sales are disliked (makruh) due to external factors such as harm or conflict with obligations, the sales themselves are valid (sahih) because the defects are not in the core elements (rukn) or conditions (shurut) of the contract. The karahah is of the type 'tanzihiyyah' (dislike due to non-essential fault). This is an important principle in Hanafi fiqh: an act can be valid in legal effect but still disliked due to external considerations. The passage thus prevents misunderstanding that makruh implies invalidity.

Key Terms
فساد (fasad): Invalidity of a contract due to a defect in its essential elements or conditions; here distinguished from karahah.
صلب العقد (sulb al-'aqd): The substance or core of the contract, including offer and acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the defect is in the substance of the contract
B) Because the defect is external and not in the core or conditions
C) Because the sale is a recommended act
D) Because the Prophet allowed it

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a sale is not invalidated by karahah; it remains valid as long as the defect does not affect the contract's core or conditions.

Permissibility of Auction Sales (Bai' Man Yazid)
Confirms legality of auction sales with hadith and necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bai' man yazid, cite the prophetic evidence, and explain why it is permissible despite potential resemblance to prohibited sales.

Core Idea
Auction sales are permissible because the Prophet himself conducted them and they serve the poor's need.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common commercial practice: selling to the highest bidder. While some might suspect it involves prohibited uncertainty (gharar) or resembles the pre-Islamic sale of munabadhah, the Hanafi school affirms its legality based on explicit prophetic precedent and practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The author begins with 'la ba'sa' (no harm), which in Hanafi fiqh indicates permissibility (ibahah). The ruling is that bai' man yazid is allowed without any dislike (karahah).
Note the positive phrasing: not just 'ja'iz' but 'la ba'sa' – a stronger affirmation of permissibility.
2
Locate the Prophetic Evidence
The text cites a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) sold a cup (qadah) and a coarse blanket (jalsa) by bidding. This action (fi'l) is the primary evidence. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's actions are generally legislative (ta'sisi) and indicate permissibility.
The hadith is reported in various collections; its chain is authentic (sahih) but ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Analyze the Rationale (Hikmah)
The second evidence is 'the sale of the poor' and 'necessity calls for it'. This shows that the ruling is not just based on a text but also on a rational consideration: auction allows the poor to obtain a fair price for their goods.
This rationale does not make the ruling contingent on need; it reinforces the permissibility.
4
Address Potential Objections
Some might compare bai' man yazid to the prohibited bai' al-munabadhah (where each party throws a garment without inspection). The key distinction: in auction, the price is determined through open bidding, not through a hidden or uncertain mechanism.
The Hanafi school explicitly distinguishes the two, as stated in earlier 'kitab al-buyu' passages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا باس ببيع من يزيد وتفسيره ماذكرنا وقد صح ان النبى باع قد حاو جلسنا ببيع من يزيد ولانه بيع الفقراء والحاجة ماسة اليه. اور ایسی بیچ میں مضائقہ نہیں ہے کہ کون زیادہ دیتا ہے اور اس کی تفسیر وہی ہے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے اور بیج ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ایک پیالہ اور ایک موٹی کملی بیچ من یزید کے طور پر فروخت کیں اور اس لئے کہ یہ بیع فقیروں کی بیع ہے اور اسکی جانب ضرورت داعی ہے۔ تشریح بیع من بزید بلا کراہت جائز ہے اور بیع من یزید کی تفسیر سابق میں گذر چکی کہ کسی چیز کو نیلام کرنا اور بولی لگانا ، اس کا جواز
He said: And there is no harm in a sale by bidding (bai' man yazid). And its interpretation is what we have mentioned. And it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sold a cup and a coarse blanket by bidding. And because it is the sale of the poor, and necessity calls for it. [Urdu: And there is no harm in such a sale where one asks who gives more, and its interpretation is what we have mentioned. And it is proven that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sold a cup and a thick blanket by bidding. And because this is the sale of the poor, and necessity calls for it. Commentary: Sale by bidding without karahah is permissible. And the interpretation of bai' man yazid has already passed: that auctioning an item and bidding is its permissibility.]

Commentary
This passage affirms the validity and permissibility of auction-style sales (bai' man yazid), where an item is sold to the highest bidder. The proof is a hadith that the Prophet himself conducted such a sale (selling a cup and a blanket by bidding). The commentator notes that it is particularly beneficial for the poor who need to get the best price for their goods. There is no karahah in this type of sale, unlike the previously mentioned disliked sales. The earlier interpretation (in the text) likely defined the term. The sale is valid and recommended as a means of fair pricing.

Key Terms
بيع من يزيد (bai' man yazid): A sale where the seller offers an item to bidders, and it is sold to the one who offers the highest price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Bai' man yazid (auction) is permissible in the Hanafi school based on the Prophet's own practice and its benefit to the poor.

Why Karahah Does Not Invalidate a Sale
Explains why these sales are makruh but not fasid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a sale that is makruh remains valid in Hanafi fiqh and distinguish between fasad (invalidity) and karahah (dislike).

Core Idea
A sale is not invalidated by an external defect; only defects in the contract's essence or conditions cause invalidity.

In the previous sections of the chapter, the author listed several sales that are disliked (makruh). A student might wonder: if these sales are disliked, are they also invalid? This passage clarifies a key Hanafi principle: a sale can be valid yet disliked. The reason is that the defect causing the dislike is external to the core of the contract and its conditions of validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The author states that all the mentioned sales are makruh, but the karahah does not make the sale fasid (invalid). The sale remains valid (sahih).
Karahah here is tanzihiyyah (recommended to avoid), not tahrimiyyah (prohibited).
2
Understand the reason
The reason given: 'fasad (invalidity) lies in a meaning that is external and additional, not in the essence (salb) of the contract nor in its conditions of validity (shurut al-sihhah).' This means the defect is not inherent to the contract's pillars or conditions.
The defect is in something adjacent to the contract, like the timing or circumstance.
3
Distinguish between salb and shurut
Salb al-'aqd refers to the essential elements: offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). Shurut al-sihhah are the conditions that must be present for the contract to be valid, such as capacity and free consent. Both are intact here.
If a defect existed in either, the contract would be fasid or batil.
4
Apply to examples
Consider the sale at the time of the Friday adhan mentioned earlier. The sale is valid because the offer and acceptance are sound and all conditions are met, but it is disliked due to the timing which is a secondary, external factor.
The ruling applies to all similar cases where the defect is outside the core of the contract.

مذکورہ بیوع میں کراہت کی وجہ قال كل ذالك يكره لما ذكرنا ولا يفسد به البيع لان الفساد في معنى خارج زائد لا في صلب العقد ولا في شرائط الصحة ترجمہ اور یہ سب بیوع مکروہ ہیں اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے اور کراہت کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ فسادا ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے ہے جو خارج سے زائد ہے صاب عقد میں نہیں ہے اور نہ شرائ کا صحت میں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اول فصل سے لے کر اب تک جتنی بیوع مذکور ہوئیں سب مکروہ ہیں اور کراہت کی وجہ سے بیچ فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ فساد یعنی فتح ایسے معنی میں ہے جو عقد سے خارج ہے البتہ عقد کے مجاور ہے صلب عقد اور شر انکا صحت میں کوئی قباحت نہیں ہے اور جو قباحت معنی خارج مجاور میں ہوتی ہے اس کی وجہ سے بیع مکروہ ہوتی ہے فاسد نہیں ہوتی اس لئے مذکورہ تمام صورتوں میں مگر وہ ہو گی فاسد نہ ہوگی۔
The reason for karahah in the mentioned sales: He said: All of these are makruh due to what we have mentioned, and the sale is not nullified by it because the fasad (invalidity) lies in a meaning that is external and additional, not in the essence (salb) of the contract nor in its conditions of validity. Translation: And all these sales are makruh due to the proof we have mentioned, and due to the karahah the sale does not become fasid because fasad is due to a meaning external and additional, not in the essence of the contract nor in its conditions of validity. Explanation: Sahib Quduri says: From the beginning of the chapter until now, all the sales mentioned are makruh, and due to the karahah the sale does not become fasid because fasad is a meaning external to the contract, adjacent to it, but there is no defect in the essence of the contract or its conditions of validity. The defect in the external adjacent meaning makes the sale makruh, not fasid. Therefore, in all the mentioned cases, the sale is makruh, not fasid.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling that explains a key principle: karahah (dislike) in a sale does not render it fasid (invalid). The author, Quduri, makes a general statement covering all the sales discussed from the beginning of the chapter (such as selling at the time of Friday adhan, etc.). These sales are all makruh, but they remain valid. The reason is that the defect causing the karahah is 'external and additional' (ma'na kharaj za'id) to the contract itself. It does not affect the essential components (salb) of the contract or its conditions of validity. The 'defect' is something adjacent to the contract, like the timing or circumstance, not an inherent flaw. Therefore, the sale is valid but disliked. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh: karahah tanzihiyyah does not affect the legal effect of the contract.

Key Terms
فساد (fasad): Invalidity of a contract due to a defect in the essence or conditions. Here it is distinguished from karahah.
صلب العقد (salb al-'aqd): The essence or core of the contract, i.e., offer and acceptance.
شرائط الصحة (shurut al-sihhah): Conditions of validity that must be present for the contract to be sound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the karahah in the mentioned sales not make them fasid?
A) Because the defect is in the essence of the contract.
B) Because the defect is external and does not affect the core or conditions.
C) Because all sales are inherently permissible.
D) Because the seller repented after the sale.

Key Takeaway
A sale can be valid and enforceable even if it is disliked (makruh), as long as the defect is not in its essence or conditions.

Permissibility of Auction (Bay' Man Yazid) — Proof from Hadith
Proving permissibility of auction via prophetic action and benefit to poor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on auction (bay' man yazid) and explain the prophetic action that establishes its permissibility.

Core Idea
Auction is permissible because the Prophet himself sold goods by bidding.

This lesson derives the permissibility of auction (bay' man yazid) from a specific hadith where the Prophet auctioned a blanket and a bowl belonging to a poor Ansari. By examining the prophetic practice and the benefit to the seller, the Hanafi school affirms auction as a valid and beneficial sale. We will walk through the hadith, extract the legal principle, and see how it applies to modern charity auctions.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Identify the key events: the Prophet asks for bids, encourages higher bids, and sells to the highest bidder. Note that he does not criticize the process but uses the proceeds to help the man earn a living.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud; it is a hadith ahad with zanni thubut.
2
Identify the act ruled upon
The act is the sale of an item by calling for bids (auction). The ruling derived is permissibility (jawaz).
3
Analyze the dalil
The Prophet's action is the dalil. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates permissibility (ibaha) unless there is evidence of prohibition. Also, his explicit request for higher bids affirms the practice.
Wajh al-dalalah: the Prophet did not prohibit the bidding process; he initiated it.
4
Consider the secondary proof
The author adds that auction benefits the poor by maximizing profit. This is a maslaha (public interest) argument reinforcing permissibility.
This aligns with istihsan, but the primary proof is the hadith.
5
Conclude the ruling
Auction (bay' man yazid) is ja'iz (permissible). It is not gharar because the object is present and the price is determined by mutual consent through bidding.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

مہاری مدظلہ کے ساتھ تھا بہار کے کسی گاؤں میں ایک بیوہ غریب عورت نے مرغی کا ایک انڈا پیش کیا۔ حضرت موصوف نے اس کو نیلام کیا تو وہ تین سو کچھ روپے کا فروخت ہوا بغیر بیج من یزید کے یہ انڈا شاید اس قیمت پر فروخت نہ ہوتا حاصل یہ کہ بیچ من یزید میں فقرا ء کا فائدہ ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کی اجازت بلا کر بہت دی گئی ہے۔
It is established from the hadith of Anas: A man from the Ansar came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) asking him. He said, 'Is there anything in your house?' He replied, 'Yes, a blanket which we partly wear and partly spread, and a bowl from which we drink water.' He said, 'Bring them to me.' So he brought them. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) took them and said, 'Who will buy these?' A man said, 'I will take them for a dirham.' He said, 'Who will give more than a dirham?' twice or thrice. A man said, 'I will take them for two dirhams.' So he gave them to him and took the two dirhams, and gave them to the Ansari and said, 'Buy food with one dirham and give it to your family, and buy an axe with the other and bring it to me.' He brought it, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) fixed a handle in it with his own hand, then said, 'Go, cut firewood and sell it, and do not let me see you for fifteen days.' The man went cutting and selling firewood, and came back having earned ten dirhams. He bought a garment with some and food with some. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'This is better for you than that begging should come as a spot on your face on the Day of Resurrection. Asking is not permissible except for three: one who is extremely poor, one who is burdened with a heavy debt, or one who is liable for blood money and cannot pay it.' (Abu Dawud) Explanation: An Ansari man came to the Prophet asking. He asked, 'Is there anything in your house?' He replied, 'Yes, a blanket we partly wear and partly spread, and a bowl we drink water from.' He said, 'Bring them to me.' He brought them. The Prophet took them and said, 'Who will buy these?' A man said, 'I will take them for one dirham.' He said, 'Who will give more than one dirham?' twice or thrice. A man said, 'I will take them for two dirhams.' He gave them to him and took the two dirhams. He gave them to the Ansari and said, 'Buy food with one dirham and give it to your family, and buy an axe with the other and bring it to me.' He brought the axe, and the Prophet fixed a handle in it with his own hand, then said, 'Go cut firewood and bring it, and do not let me see you for fifteen days.' That man went, cut firewood, brought and sold it. Then he came and had earned ten dirhams. He bought a garment with some and food with some. The Prophet said, 'This is better for you than that you should come on the Day of Resurrection with a spot on your face. Asking is not permissible except for three: one who is extremely poor and afflicted, one who is burdened with a heavy debt, or one who has committed bloodshed and is liable for blood money, then he may ask out of necessity.' From this hadith it is understood that selling by auction is permissible; otherwise why would the Lawgiver do that? The second proof is that bay' man yazid (sale to the highest bidder) is a means for the poor, and it is needed to maximize benefit for the poor. Therefore this sale is permissible. I remember that on the occasion of the centenary gathering for raising capital, I was with my respected teacher Mawlana Muhammad Hussain Sahib Mahari (may his shadow be prolonged) on a journey to Bihar. In a village of Bihar, a poor widow woman offered a hen's egg. The respected teacher auctioned it, and it sold for three hundred and some rupees. Without bay' man yazid, this egg would probably not have sold at that price. In short, bay' man yazid benefits the poor, therefore its permission is widely given.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage provides a proof for the permissibility of auction (bay' man yazid) in the Hanafi school. The author first cites a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) auctioned a blanket and a bowl belonging to a poor Ansari. The Prophet asked for bids, encouraged higher bids, and sold the items to the highest bidder, then used the proceeds to buy an axe for the man to earn a living. This action demonstrates the permissibility of auction. The author then adds a second rational argument: auction benefits the poor by maximizing profit. He supports this with an anecdote from his own teacher, who auctioned a hen's egg for far more than its ordinary price, showing the practical benefit. The conclusion is that auction (bay' man yazid) is a permissible and beneficial transaction.

Key Terms
نیلام (nīlām): Auction; sale to the highest bidder, as performed by the Prophet in the hadith.
بیع من یزید (bay' man yazīd): Sale of him who increases; a sale where goods are offered to the highest bidder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What is the primary evidence from the lesson for the permissibility of auction?
A) The Quranic verse on trade
B) Consensus of the Companions
C) The Prophet's action of auctioning a blanket and bowl
D) The benefit to the seller

Key Takeaway
Auction (bay' man yazid) is permissible in Hanafi fiqh, established by prophetic practice and the benefit to the poor.
