Legitimacy of Iqalah and Ruling on Condition of Increase or Decrease
Defines iqalah, provides proof from hadith and consensus, and states the ruling when a condition of more or less is stipulated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqalah, cite the hadith proof, and apply the rule that a condition of increase or decrease is void while the iqalah remains valid with the original price.

Core Idea
Iqalah is permissible with the original price; any condition of more or less is void.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on iqalah – the cancellation of a sale by mutual consent when the seller regrets. You will learn the legal status, the proof from the Sunnah and consensus, and a key principle: if the parties stipulate a price other than the original, that condition is invalid, but the iqalah itself stands with the original price. This foundational rule protects the rescissory nature of iqalah and prevents it from being transformed into a new sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is iqalah? The text states it is permissible (ja'iz) when the buyer returns the exact original price. The hukm level is mubah, with recommendation due to the hadith reward.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are given: (1) A hadith promising that Allah will cancel the slips of one who grants iqalah to a regretful seller. (2) A rational argument: the contract is the right of both parties, so they may revoke it by mutual consent.
Consensus (ijma') is also mentioned as supporting evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies legitimacy because reward is only attached to legitimate acts. The rational argument shows that since the contract is voluntary, its dissolution by mutual consent is also valid.
4
Note the subsidiary ruling
If a condition of increase or decrease is stipulated, that condition is void (batil). The iqalah remains valid, and the parties must return the original price (mithl al-thaman al-awwal).
This distinguishes iqalah from a new sale, which would allow a different price.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم دلیل ... حدیث ہے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد ہے من اقال نبا دماً بيعته اقال الله عشر انه يوم القيامته یعنی اگر کوئی شخص بیچ کرنے کے بعد اپنے فعل پر نادم اور پشیمان ہو اور اس نے اقالہ کرنے کا ارادہ ظاہر کیا تو اگر دوسرے عاقد نے اس کی بیع کا اقالہ کر دیا یعنی بیع فسخ کر دی تو اللہ تعالی اس عاقد آخر کی لغزشوں کو بروز قیامت دور کر دے گا ۔ گویا اقالہ کرنے پر ثواب کی خبر دی ہے یا ثواب کی دعا کی ہے اور ان دونوں کا ترتب امر مشروع پر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ غیر مشروع پر پس ثابت ہوا کہ اقالہ مشروع ہے۔

فان شرط اكثر منه اواقل فالشرط باطل ويرد مثل الثمن الاول
Chapter of Iqalah. This chapter is about iqalah. Explanation: Iqalah is derived from qawl (speech) and its hamzah is for the subject, meaning to remove a previous statement. Allamah Ibn al-Humam and Allamah Badr al-Din al-Ayni said that considering iqalah derived from qawl is incorrect; the correct view is that the word iqalah is from qayl (i.e. the root has ya not waw). The proof is that it is said 'qaltu al-bay'a' (I cancelled the sale) with a kasrah on the qaf, and kasrah on the qaf occurs in hollow verbs with ya not waw. Also in the books of lexicography, the word iqalah is mentioned in the chapter of qaf with ya, not with waw. In any case, iqalah is a masdar of the af'al form meaning to break/cancel. The chapter on iqalah is placed after the chapters on invalid and disliked sales because an invalid or disliked sale must be returned due to sin, and return occurs through iqalah. Legal status of iqalah: 'Al-iqalah ja'izah fi al-bay'i bi-mithli al-thamani al-awwal' (Iqalah is permissible in sale with the like of the first price) because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever cancels the sale of a regretful person, Allah will cancel his slips on the Day of Judgment,' and because the contract is their right, so they have the power to raise it to fulfill their need. Translation: Iqalah in sale is permissible with the like of the first price because the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: Whoever gives iqalah to a regretful person for his sale, Allah will remove his missteps on the Day of Judgment. And because the contract of sale is the right of both parties, so they have full authority to remove it to fulfill their need. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri says that iqalah of a sale is permissible with the like of the first price, and there is consensus of all Muslims on the permissibility of iqalah. Proof: The hadith of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ: 'Man aqala nadiman bay'atahu aqala Allahu 'atharatihi yawma al-qiyamah' meaning if a person regrets his act after selling and expresses intention to get iqalah, and the other party cancels the sale, then Allah will remove the other party's slips on the Day of Judgment. So he informed of reward or prayed for reward, and both follow from the command being legitimate, not illegitimate, so it is established that iqalah is legitimate. Second proof: Iqalah is the name for ending a contract, and the contract is the right of the two contractors because it is concluded by their mutual consent. So when the contract is their right and concluded by their consent, they have full authority to raise it due to need. Ruling on condition of decrease or increase from the first price: 'Fa-in sharata akthara minhu aw aqalla fa-al-shartu batilun wa yuruddu mithla al-thamani al-awwal' (If he stipulates more than it or less, the condition is void, and he returns the like of the first price).
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It opens the chapter on iqalah (cancellation of a sale). The commentator first discusses the etymology of the word iqalah, whether it derives from qawl (speech) or qayl (a hollow verb with ya). He sides with those who say it is from qayl, as the verb 'qala al-bay'a' (he cancelled the sale) uses a kasra on the qaf, consistent with hollow verbs of the ya variety. The chapter is placed after discussions of invalid and disliked sales because those sales must be undone, and iqalah is one means of undoing them. The core ruling is stated in the Arabic matn: 'Al-iqalah ja'izah fi al-bay'i bi-mithli al-thamani al-awwal' – iqalah is permissible only when the buyer returns the exact same price as originally paid. The proof is twofold: first, a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ promising that Allah will cancel the slips of anyone who grants iqalah to a regretful seller; second, a rational argument that the contract is the right of the parties, so they have the authority to revoke it by mutual consent. The commentator stresses that the hadith indicates the act is legitimate (mashru') because the promised reward (either akhbar or du'a) only attaches to legitimate actions. There is also a mention of ijma' (consensus) on permissibility. Then a subsidiary ruling is given: if the parties stipulate a price higher or lower than the original when doing iqalah, the stipulation is void, and they must still return exactly the original price (mithl al-thaman al-awwal). This is because iqalah is fundamentally a rescission, not a new sale, so any variation in price is invalid. The text then proceeds to a detailed dispute about the legal nature of iqalah (faskh vs. sale), which is covered in the next lesson.

Key Terms
إقالة (iqalah): Cancellation or rescission of a sale contract by mutual consent, returning the sold item and price as they were, typically when the seller regrets the sale.
ثمن الأول (al-thaman al-awwal): The original price paid at the time of the sale, which must be returned in iqalah without addition or subtraction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two parties agree to cancel a sale through iqalah but stipulate that the buyer returns 10% less than the original price, what is the ruling according to this passage?
A) The iqalah is valid and the reduced price applies.
B) The stipulation is void, but the iqalah is valid and the original price must be returned.
C) The entire iqalah is void because the condition is invalid.
D) The iqalah becomes a new sale at the reduced price.

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is a recommended cancellation of sale with the exact original price; any condition to pay more or less is void.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Iqalah: Faskh or Sale?
Presents three Hanafi imams' positions on whether iqalah is a rescission or a new sale, with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the legal nature of iqalah (faskh vs. bay') and explain the proof of each imam.

Core Idea
Iqalah is a rescission (faskh) in Hanafi law, not a new sale, except for third parties.

This lesson explores a fundamental intra-Hanafi dispute: when a sale is cancelled by mutual agreement (iqalah), is it a rescission of the original contract (faskh) or a brand new sale (bay')? The three major Hanafi imams—Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—each offer distinct analyses of the same transaction, relying on linguistic principles, definitions, and practical consequences. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between the legal nature of an act and its effects, a key skill in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
The central issue is the legal classification of iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale): is it a rescission (faskh) of the original contract, or a new independent sale (bay')? The answer affects many subsidiary rulings such as the effect of destruction, defect, and pre-emption.
This is not about permissibility (all agree iqalah is allowed) but about legal nature.
2
State the three positions
List the positions of Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Note the order of priority in each: Abu Hanifah: first faskh, if impossible then void. Abu Yusuf: first sale, if impossible then faskh, else void. Muhammad: first faskh, if impossible then sale, else void.
The text presents Abu Hanifah's view as 'al-asl' (the principle), indicating its weight.
3
Analyze Muhammad's proof
Muhammad argues that the word 'iqalah' linguistically means rescission (faskh), as in the phrase 'aqilni 'athrati' (forgive my slip). Words must be used in their true meaning; only when that is impossible may they be used in a probable meaning (sale). He points to third-party treatment as evidence that sale is a probable meaning.
This is a linguistic argument based on primary vs. secondary usage.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf defines iqalah as an exchange of property by mutual consent, which is the very definition of sale (bay'). He supports this by noting that iqalah attracts the rulings of a sale: void by destruction of the commodity, return for defect, and establishment of pre-emption (shuf'ah).
This is a definitional argument focusing on the objective characteristics of the transaction.
5
Analyze Abu Hanifah's proof
Abu Hanifah insists that the word 'iqalah' indicates rescission, and words must be given their true implications. The word cannot bear its opposite (sale). Therefore, if faskh is impossible, the contract is void, not converted to a sale. The treatment as a sale regarding third parties is a necessity (ownership must be established), not a linguistic shift.
Abu Hanifah prioritizes linguistic principle over consequentialist reasoning.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The text presents Abu Hanifah's view as 'al-asl' and concludes with his stronger linguistic argument. Therefore, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that iqalah is faskh regarding the parties and a new sale only regarding third parties; if faskh is impossible, it is void.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاصل ان الاقالة فسخ في حق المتعاقدين بيع جديد فى حق غيرهما الا ان لا يمكن جعله فسخا فتبطل وهذا عندابي حنيفة وعندابي يوسف هو بيع الا ان لا يمكن جعله بيعا فيجعل فسخا الا ان لا يمكن فتبطل وعند محمد هو فسخ الا اذا تعذر جعله فسخا فيجعل بيعا الا ان لا يمكن فيبطل لمحمد ان اللفظ للفسخ والرفع ومنه يقال اقلني عشرتي فيوفر عليه قضيته واذا تعذر يحمل على محتمله وهو البيع الا ترى انه بيع في حق الثالث ولا بي يوسف انه مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضى وهذا هو حد البيع ولهذا يبطل بهلاك السلعة ويرد بالعيب و تثبت به الشفعة وهذا احكام البيع ولابي حنيفة ان اللفظ ينبئى عن الفسخ والرفع كما قلنا والاصل اعمال الالفاظ فى مقتضياتها الحقيقية ولا يحتمل ابتداء العقد ليحمل عليه عند تعذره لا نه ضده واللفظ لا يحتمل ضده فتعين البطلان وكونه بيعا فى حق الثالث امر ضرورى لا نه يثبت به مثل حكم البيع وهو الملک لا مقتضى الصيغة اذا لا ولاية لهما على غيرهما
And the principle is that iqalah is a rescission (faskh) in the right of the two contractors, a new sale in the right of others, unless it is not possible to make it a rescission, then it becomes void. This is according to Abu Hanifah. According to Abu Yusuf, it is a sale, unless it is not possible to make it a sale, then it is made a rescission; unless it is not possible, then it becomes void. According to Muhammad, it is a rescission, unless making it a rescission is not possible, then it is made a sale; unless it is not possible, then it becomes void. For Muhammad is that the word (iqalah) is for rescission and removal, and from it is said 'aqilni 'athrati' (cancel my slip), so the word is given its full meaning. When it is not possible, it is carried to its probable meaning which is sale. Do you not see that it is a sale in the right of a third party? For Abu Yusuf is that it is an exchange of property for property by mutual consent, and this is the definition of sale. For this reason, it is void by destruction of the commodity, it is returned due to defect, and pre-emption is established by it – these are rulings of sale. For Abu Hanifah is that the word indicates rescission and removal as we said, and the principle is to use words in their true implications, and it cannot bear initiating a contract to be carried on it when [the true meaning] is not possible because it is its opposite, and the word does not bear its opposite. So voidness is determined. And it being a sale in the right of a third party is a necessary matter because that party is established a ruling similar to sale, which is ownership, not due to the wording since they have no authority over others.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute presented in the commentary. After establishing the permissibility of iqalah and the ruling on condition of price variation, the text delves into the fundamental disagreement among the three major Hanafi imams about the legal nature of iqalah: is it a rescission (faskh) of the original contract or a new sale (bay')? The 'asl' (principle) stated first is that iqalah is faskh in the rights of the original parties but a new sale regarding third parties. If making it a rescission is impossible, it becomes void. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifah. Imam Abu Yusuf holds the opposite: iqalah is primarily a sale, and only if it cannot be a sale is it treated as a rescission; if neither possible, void. Imam Muhammad's view is similar to Abu Hanifah's: it is faskh, but if faskh is impossible, it becomes a sale; if sale also impossible, void. Each imam gives a proof: Muhammad argues from the linguistic meaning of iqalah (rescission, removal – as in the phrase 'aqilni 'athrati' meaning 'forgive my slip'), and points to the fact that it is a sale regarding third parties. Abu Yusuf argues that iqalah fits the definition of a sale (exchange of property by mutual consent) and attracts the rulings of a sale (e.g., if the commodity is destroyed, the iqalah is void; if a defect is found, it can be returned; shuf'ah pre-emption applies). Abu Hanifah insists that the word itself means rescission and removal, and a word should be used in its true meaning; it cannot bear the opposite meaning (a new sale) because that would be its opposite; if the true meaning is impossible, the contract is void, not converted to a sale. The only exception is regarding third parties, where it is treated as a sale by necessity (since the new owner's ownership is established), but this is not due to the wording but due to practical necessity. The practical consequence (thamarah) of this dispute appears in cases such as: if the commodity is destroyed before delivery in iqalah, according to Abu Yusuf the iqalah is void because it is a sale (risk passes), but according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, since it is a rescission, the destruction nullifies the rescission? Actually, each position affects rulings like the effect of destruction, defect, and pre-emption. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifah (iqalah is faskh), as this is the 'asl' stated and the commentary supports it with stronger reasoning.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract, returning both parties to their pre-contract state, as opposed to a new contract.
بيع (bay'): A sale contract: exchange of property for property by mutual consent.
إقالة (iqalah): Mutual rescission of a sale contract, returning the subject matter and price, with the legal nature disputed among imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the legal nature of iqalah?
A) It is always a new sale.
B) It is a rescission (faskh) in the rights of the parties and a new sale regarding third parties.
C) It is a rescission only.
D) It is a sale that can become a rescission if necessary.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that iqalah is a rescission (faskh) between the original parties, and only treated as a sale regarding third parties out of necessity.

The Validity of Iqalah and the Ruling on Stipulating a Different Price
Establishes validity of iqalah and the rule on price condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence for the validity of iqalah and apply the rule that a condition for a different price in iqalah is void, requiring return of the original price.

Core Idea
Iqalah is a rescission, not a new sale — only the original price must be returned.

This lesson covers the basic validity of iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale) and the critical rule that if the parties stipulate a price different from the original, the condition is void. You will learn the textual and rational proofs for iqalah and understand why the original price alone is due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proofs for iqalah
Locate the hadith: 'Whoever rescinds the sale of a regretful person, Allah will remove his stumbles on the Day of Resurrection.' Also note the rational argument: the contract is the right of the parties, so they can revoke it by mutual consent.
These proofs establish iqalah as a legislated (mashru') act.
2
State the ruling on a different price condition
The passage states: 'If he stipulates more or less than it, the condition is void, and he returns a price equal to the first price.' This means any deviation from the original price in iqalah is invalid.
This ruling is agreed upon by all three imams despite their differences on the nature of iqalah.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is that iqalah is a rescission (faskh) regarding the contracting parties. Therefore, only the original contract's price is relevant; a new price cannot be imposed.
If iqalah were a new sale, the stipulated price would be binding, but it is not.
4
Apply to a concrete example
Consider a sale for 1000. If the parties agree to rescind but one says 'I will return 800,' the condition is void. The seller must return exactly 1000.
This shows that the original price is the only lawful consideration in iqalah.

Source Text

(۲۴۵) كتاب البيوع اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم دلیل ... حدیث ہے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد ہے "من اقال نادما بيعته اقال الله عثرته يوم القيامة" یعنی اگر کوئی شخص بیچ کرنے کے بعد اپنے فعل پر نادم اور پشیمان ہو اور اس نے اقالہ کرنے کا ارادہ ظاہر کیا تو اگر دوسرے عاقد نے اس کی بیع کا اقالہ کر دیا یعنی بیع فسخ کر دی تو اللہ تعالی اس عاقد آخر کی لغزشوں کو بروز قیامت دور کر دے گا۔ گویا اقالہ کرنے پر اللہ کے رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ثواب کی خبر دی ہے یا ثواب کی دعا کی ہے اور ان دونوں کا ترتب امر مشروع پر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ غیر مشروع پر پس ثابت ہوا کہ اقالہ مشروع ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقالہ نام ہے عقد ختم کرنے کا اور عقد متعاقدین کا حق ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ ان دونوں کی رضامندی سے منعقد ہوا ہے پس جب عقد عاقدین کا حق ہے اور انھیں کی رضا مندی سے منعقد ہوا ہے تو ضرورت کے پیش نظر ان دونوں کو اس کے رفع کرنے کا بھی پورا پورا اختیار ہے۔

فان شرط اكثر منه اواقل فالشرط باطل ويرد مثل الثمن الاول والاصل ان الاقالة فسخ في حق المتعاقدين بيع جديد فى حق غيرهما الا ان لا يمكن جعله فسخا فتبطل وهذا عندابي حنيفة وعندابي يوسف هو بيع الا ان لا يمكن جعله بيعا فيجعل فسخا الا ان لا يمكن فتبطل وعند محمد هو فسخ الا اذا تعذر جعله فسخا فيجعل بيعا الا ان لا يمكن فيبطل لمحمد ان اللفظ للفسخ والرفع ومنه يقال اقلني عثرتي فيوفر عليه قضيته واذا تعذر يحمل على محتمله وهو البيع الا ترى انه بيع في حق الثالث ولا بي يوسف انه مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضى وهذا هو حد البيع ولهذا يبطل بهلاك السلعة ويرد بالعيب و تثبت به الشفعة وهذا احكام البيع ولابي حنيفة ان اللفظ ينبئى عن الفسخ والرفع كما قلنا والاصل اعمال الالفاظ فى مقتضياتها الحقيقية ولا يحتمل ابتداء العقد ليحمل عليه عند تعذره لا نه ضده واللفظ لا يحتمل ضده فتعين البطلان وكونه بيعا فى حق الثالث امر ضرورى لا نه يثبت به مثل حكم البيع وهو الملک لا مقتضى الصيغة اذا لا ولاية لهما على غيرهما

ترجمہ ۔ پس اگر ثمن اول سے زیادہ کی یا کم کی شرط کی تو شرط باطل ہے اور بائع ثمن اول کے مثل واپس کرے اور اصل یہ ہے کہ اقالہ عاقدین کے حق میں فسخ ہے ( اور ) ان دونوں کے علاوہ کے حق میں بیع جدید ہے لیکن اگر اس فسخ کو فسخ قرار دینا ممکن نہ ہو تو اقالہ باطل ہوگا یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقالہ بیع ہے لیکن اگر اس کو بیع قرار دینا ممکن نہ ہو تو فسخ قرار دیا جائے گا لیکن اگر فسخ قرار دینا ممکن نہ ہو تو اقالہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اقالہ فسخ ہے مگر جبکہ اس کو فسخ قرار دینا متعذر ہو تو بیع قرار دیا جائے گا لیکن اگر بیع قرار دینا ممکن نہ ہو تو اقالہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اقالہ لغت میں نسخ اور دور کرنے کے معنی میں آتا ہے اسی سے کہا جاتا ہے میری لغزش معاف کر دے پس لفظ اقالہ کو وہ معنی بھر پور دیئے جائیں گے جو لفظ کا مقتضی ہے اور جب یہ معنیٰ متعذر ہوں تو اقالہ اپنے محتمل معنی یعنی بیع پر محمول کیا جائے گا کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ اقالہ تیسرے کے حق میں بیع جدید ہے اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقالہ باہمی رضا مندی سے مال کا مال کے عوض تبادلہ کرنا ہے اور یہی بیع کی تعریف ہے اس وجہ سے مبیع کے ہلاک ہونے سے (۲۴۶) كتاب البيوع اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو برای جلد بقر اقالہ باطل ہو جاتا ہے اور عیب کی وجہ سے بیع واپس کی جاتی ہے اور اقالہ کی وجہ سے حق شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے حالانکہ یہ سب احکام بیع ہیں۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اقالہ فسخ اور رفع کی خبر دیتا ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے کہا اور اصل یہ ہے کہ الفاظ کو ان کے معنی حقیقیہ میں عمل دلایا جائے اور لفظ اقالہ ابتدائے عقد کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا تا کہ فسخ متعذر ہونے کے وقت ابتدائے عقد پر محمول کیا جائے ۔ اس لئے کہ عقد بیع فسخ کی ضد ہے اور لفظ اپنی ضد کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے اسلئے باطل ہو نا متعین ہو گیا۔ اور اقالہ کا تیسرے کے حق میں بیع ہونا ایک امر ضروری ہے کیونکہ اقالہ سے حکم بیع کے مثل یعنی ملکیت ثابت ہوتی ہے نہ کہ صیغہ اقالہ کا مقتضی، یہ بیع ہے اس لئے کہ بائع اور مشتری کی ولایت غیر پر نہیں ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر اقالہ میں ثمن اول سے زیادہ کی شرط کی یا کم کی شرط کی تو یہ شرط باطل ہے اور بائع پر ثمن اول واپس کرنا واجب ہے مثلاً کوئی چیز ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کی گئی اور بائع نے ثمن پر اور مشتری نے مبیع پر قبضہ کر لیا تو اب اگر اقالہ کرنا ہو تو بائع پر ایک ہزار روپیہ واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا ایک ہزار روپیہ سے زائد یا کم کی شرط لگانا درست نہ ہو گا چنانچہ اگر بائع نے دو سو روپیہ کم دینے کی شرط کی یا مشتری نے دو سو روپیہ زائد لینے کی شرط کی تو یہ شرط باطل ہوگی اور بائع پر فقط ایک ہزار روپیہ واپس کرنالازم ہوگا۔

امام ابو حنیفہ کا مسلک .... صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اقالہ متعاقدین کے حق میں فسخ بیع ہے اور ان دونوں کے علاوہ کے حق میں بیع جدید ہے۔ بیع عاقدین کے حق میں فسخ ہونے کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ بائع پر فقط ثمن کا واپس کرنا واجب ہے اور ثمن سے زائد یا کم کی جو شرط لگائی تھی وہ باطل ہے اگر اقالہ ان دونوں کے حق میں فسخ نہ ہوتا بلکہ بیع ہوتا تو جو کچھ انھوں نے متعین کیا تھا خواہ ثمن اول سے زائد ہوتا یا ثمن اول سے کم ہوتا تو وہ واجب ہوتا کیونکہ بیع میں عاقدین جو ثمن متعین کرتے ہیں وہی واجب ہوتا ہے اس کے علاوہ واجب نہیں ہوتا پس اقالہ میں بائع پر ثمن اول کا واجب ہونا اور عاقدین کا متعین کردہ واجب نہ ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اقالہ عاقدین کے حق میں فسخ بیع ہے اور بیع جدید نہیں ہے۔ دوسرا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ اقالہ شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتا اگر اقالہ ان دونوں کے حق میں بیع ہوتا تو شروط فاسدہ سے باطل ہو جاتا۔ جیسا کہ بیع شروط فاسدہ سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے پس اقالہ کا شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہ ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اقالہ عاقدین کے حق میں فسخ بیع ہے بیع نہیں ہے۔ تیسرا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ اقالہ کرنے کے بعد اگر بائع نے مشتری سے مبیع واپس نہیں لی بلکہ وہ مبیع اسی مشتری کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دی تو یہ بیع جائز ہے اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اقالہ عاقدین کے حق میں فسخ بیع ہے کیونکہ اگر اقالہ عاقدین کے حق میں بیع ہوتا تو مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اس کا بیچنا لازم آتا حالانکہ مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مشتری کے لئے اس کا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اور اگر اقالہ کے بعد مبیع پر قبضہ کئے بغیر بائع نے مشتری کے علاوہ دوسرے کسی آدمی کے ہاتھ بیع کی تو یہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عاقدین کے علاوہ کے حق میں اقالہ بیع جدید ہے اور بیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچنا چونکہ جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے بائع کا (جو اقالہ میں مشتری ہے) مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچنا جائز نہ ہوگا اور اقالہ، غیر عاقدین کے حق میں بیع جدید ہے اس کا فائدہ اس مثال میں ظاہر ہو گا کہ ایک آدمی نے مکان خریدا پھر شفیع نے حق شفعہ کا دعوی نہ کر کے اپنا حق چھوڑ دیا پھر عاقدین نے اقالہ کیا اور مکان بائع کی ملک میں آگیا تو وہی شفیع اگر شفعہ کا مطالبہ کرنا چاہے تو اس کو یہ اختیار ہے یعنی شفیع شفعہ طلب کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ شفیع کے حق میں اقالہ بیع جدید ہے گویا مشتری نے بائع کو وہی مکان فروخت کر دیا ہے جو اس سے
[PAGE_246] 245 Kitab al-Buyu'. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 8. Evidence... There is a hadith, the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'Whoever rescinds the sale of a regretful person, Allah will remove his stumbles on the Day of Resurrection.' That is, if a person after selling regrets and shows intention to rescind, and the other contracting party rescinds the sale (i.e., annuls the sale), then Allah will remove the lapses of that last contracting party on the Day of Resurrection. So, the Prophet (PBUH) informed of reward or prayed for reward upon doing iqalah, and both are attached to a legislated matter, not an unlegislated one. Thus it is proven that iqalah is legislated. The second evidence is that iqalah is the name of terminating the contract, and the contract is the right of the contracting parties, because it was concluded by their mutual consent. So since the contract is their right and was concluded by their consent, they have full authority to revoke it when necessary. 

'If he stipulates more or less than it, the condition is void, and he returns a price equal to the first price. The principle is that iqalah is a rescission (faskh) regarding the contracting parties and a new sale regarding others, unless it is impossible to make it a rescission, then it becomes void.' This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, it is a sale, unless it is impossible to make it a sale, then it is made a rescission, unless impossible, then it becomes void. According to Muhammad, it is a rescission, unless it is impossible to make it a rescission, then it is made a sale, unless impossible, then it becomes void. Muhammad's evidence is that the word 'iqalah' in language means annulment and removal; hence it is said 'forgive my stumble' and his affair is forgiven him. When that is impossible, it is carried to its probable meaning, which is sale. Do you not see that it is a sale regarding a third party? Abu Yusuf's evidence is that it is an exchange of property by mutual consent, and this is the definition of sale; therefore it is invalidated by the destruction of the commodity, and it is returned due to defect, and preemption is established by it, and these are rulings of a sale. Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the word indicates annulment and removal as we said, and the principle is to apply words according to their real implications. The word 'iqalah' does not bear the meaning of initiating a contract to be carried upon it when annulment is impossible, because it is its opposite, and a word does not bear its opposite. So voidness is determined. And its being a sale regarding a third party is a necessary matter because by it a ruling similar to sale is established, namely ownership, not because of the expression of iqalah, since they have no authority over others. 

Translation: So if he stipulates more than the first price or less, the condition is void and the seller returns the like of the first price. The principle is that iqalah is a rescission regarding the contracting parties and a new sale regarding others. But if it is not possible to make it a rescission, then iqalah will be void. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, iqalah is a sale, but if it is not possible to make it a sale, then it will be made a rescission, but if it is not possible to make it a rescission, then iqalah becomes void. According to Imam Muhammad, iqalah is a rescission, but when it is impossible to make it a rescission, it will be made a sale, but if it is not possible to make it a sale, then iqalah becomes void. Imam Muhammad's evidence is that the word 'iqalah' in language means annulment and removal; hence it is said 'forgive my stumble'. So the word 'iqalah' will be given its full meaning that the word requires. When this meaning is impossible, iqalah is carried upon its probable meaning, which is sale. Do you not see that iqalah is a new sale regarding a third party? Abu Yusuf's evidence is that iqalah is an exchange of property by mutual consent, and this is the definition of sale. For this reason, iqalah is invalidated by the destruction of the commodity, and it is returned due to defect, and preemption is established by iqalah, whereas all these are rulings of a sale. And Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the word 'iqalah' informs of annulment and removal as we said, and the principle is that words are applied according to their real meanings. The word 'iqalah' does not bear the meaning of initiating a contract to be carried upon it when annulment is impossible, because a sale contract is the opposite of annulment, and a word does not bear its opposite. So voidness is determined. And iqalah's being a sale regarding a third party is a necessary matter because by iqalah a ruling similar to sale is established, namely ownership, not because of the expression of iqalah, since the seller and buyer have no authority over others. 

Explanation of the case: If in iqalah a condition of more than the first price or less is stipulated, then this condition is void, and the seller must return the first price. For example, something was sold for one thousand rupees, and the seller took possession of the price and the buyer took possession of the commodity. Now if iqalah is to be done, the seller must return one thousand rupees. Stipulating more or less than one thousand rupees is not valid. So if the seller stipulates to give two hundred rupees less, or the buyer stipulates to take two hundred rupees more, this condition is void, and the seller is only required to return one thousand rupees. 

Imam Abu Hanifa's position: The author of Hidaya said that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, iqalah regarding the two contracting parties is a rescission of the sale, and regarding others it is a new sale. The benefit of it being a rescission regarding the two contracting parties is that the seller is only required to return the price, and the condition of more or less is void. If iqalah were a sale regarding them, then whatever they specified, whether more or less than the first price, would be obligatory, because in a sale the price that the parties specify is what becomes obligatory, not anything else. Thus, the obligation of returning only the first price, and not the specified amount, is evidence that iqalah regarding the parties is a rescission, not a new sale. The second benefit is that iqalah is not invalidated by invalid conditions. If iqalah were a sale regarding them, invalid conditions would invalidate it, just as a sale is invalidated by invalid conditions. So iqalah not being invalidated by invalid conditions is evidence that iqalah regarding the parties is a rescission, not a sale. The third benefit is that after iqalah, if the seller does not take back the commodity from the buyer but sells the same commodity to that same buyer, this sale is valid. This also indicates that iqalah regarding the parties is a rescission, because if iqalah were a sale regarding them, selling before taking possession would be necessary, whereas selling the commodity before taking possession is not permissible for the buyer. And if after iqalah, without taking possession of the commodity, the seller sells it to someone other than the buyer, this is not permissible. Because regarding others, iqalah is a new sale, and selling before taking possession is not permissible, so the seller (who is the buyer in the iqalah) selling before taking possession is not permissible. And iqalah regarding non-parties is a new sale. Its benefit appears in this example: A man bought a house, then the neighbor with preemption waived his right without claiming it. Then the parties did iqalah, and the house came into the seller's ownership. Now if that (original) neighbor (shafi') wants to claim preemption, he has that right, because regarding the shafi', iqalah is a new sale, as if the buyer sold that same house to the seller.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal nature of iqalah (rescission of a sale). It first establishes the validity of iqalah using a hadith and rational reasoning, then presents the ruling when a different price is stipulated in iqalah, and finally details the differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. 

The hadith cited is a well-known one: 'Whoever rescinds the sale of a regretful person, Allah will remove his stumbles on the Day of Resurrection.' This proves that iqalah is mashru' (legislated). Additionally, since the contract is the right of the parties, they have the authority to terminate it by mutual agreement.

The core ruling is: If in iqalah a condition is made to return more or less than the original price, the condition is void and only the original price must be returned. This is based on the principle that iqalah is a rescission (faskh) between the original parties, not a new sale. The passage then explains the positions of the three imams:
- Abu Hanifa holds that iqalah is a rescission regarding the parties, and if it cannot be a rescission (due to impossibility), it becomes void. It is treated as a new sale only regarding third parties out of necessity.
- Abu Yusuf holds that iqalah is essentially a new sale (bay'), and only if it cannot be a sale is it treated as a rescission.
- Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that iqalah is essentially a rescission, but if that is impossible, it is treated as a new sale.

The passage then elaborates on the practical consequences: because iqalah is a rescission between the parties, only the original price is due (not any stipulated amount), invalid conditions do not void the iqalah, and the seller can immediately resell the commodity to the same buyer without needing to take possession. Regarding third parties (e.g., a preemptor), iqalah is treated as a new sale, so the preemptor can claim preemption even after the original parties have rescinded.

The commentary emphasizes that despite this disagreement on the nature, the ruling on the voidness of a price condition is agreed upon, and the typical Hanafi practice follows the principle that iqalah is faskh.

Key Terms
اقالة (iqālah): Rescission of a sale by mutual agreement of the parties after the contract is concluded.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of a contract, treating it as if it never existed, here specifically for the original contracting parties.
بيع (bay‘): A sale; here used as a new contract with all its rulings, as opposed to rescission.

Checkpoint
According to the text, if in iqalah a price lower than the original is stipulated, what is the ruling?
A) The iqalah is void and no price is returned.
B) The condition is void; the original price must be returned.
C) The condition is valid; the lower price is binding.
D) The iqalah becomes a new sale with the lower price.

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is a rescission, not a new sale, so any condition to return a different price is void; only the original price is due.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Is Iqalah a Rescission or a New Sale?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal nature of iqalah with thamarah al-khilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the nature of iqalah and identify the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf) of each view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa sees iqalah as faskh; Sahibayn see it as bay' — but all agree on the outcome regarding the price condition.

While the ruling on the price condition is agreed upon, the Hanafi school has an internal debate on the legal nature of iqalah: is it a rescission (faskh) or a new sale (bay')? This lesson unpacks the linguistic and analogical arguments of the three imams and shows how the difference affects practical scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions
Abu Hanifa: iqalah is faskh (rescission) regarding the parties; if faskh is impossible, it becomes void. Abu Yusuf: iqalah is a new sale (bay'); if sale impossible, it becomes faskh. Muhammad: iqalah is faskh; if faskh impossible, it becomes a sale.
All three agree on a hierarchical order: first try the default nature (faskh for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, bay' for Abu Yusuf), then fallback to the other if impossible, otherwise void.
2
Examine the linguistic and analogical proofs
Abu Hanifa argues that the word 'iqalah' linguistically means annulment, not initiation, so it cannot mean a new sale. Abu Yusuf argues that iqalah is an exchange of property by consent, which matches the definition of sale, and it carries sale rulings (e.g., void if commodity destroyed, right of preemption). Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa linguistically but allows the sale interpretation when faskh is impossible.
The dispute revolves around whether to prioritize linguistic meaning or consequential resemblance.
3
Identify the practical differences (thamarah al-khilaf)
If iqalah is faskh (Abu Hanifa): only original price due, invalid conditions do not void the iqalah, seller can resell to same buyer without possession. If iqalah is bay' (Abu Yusuf): stipulated price would be binding, invalid conditions void the iqalah, preemption is established. Muhammad's view aligns with Abu Hanifa in most cases but differs when faskh is impossible.
The most notable practical difference is regarding preemption (shuf'ah): if iqalah is a new sale, a preemptor can claim; if faskh, preemption does not arise from the rescission itself.
4
Note the agreed ruling
Despite the dispute, all three agree that if a price different from the original is stipulated, that condition is void and the original price must be returned. This shows that the ikhtilaf does not affect the core ruling on the price condition.
This agreement is why the matn presents the ruling before the dispute.

امام ابو حنیفہ کا مسلک .... صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اقالہ متعاقدین کے حق میں فسخ بیع ہے اور ان دونوں کے علاوہ کے حق میں بیع جدید ہے۔ بیع عاقدین کے حق میں فسخ ہونے کا شروط فاسدہ سے باطل ہو جاتا۔ جیسا کہ بیع شروط فاسدہ سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے پس اقالہ کا شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہ ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اقالہ عاقدین کے حق میں فسخ بیع ہے بیع نہیں ہے۔ تیسرا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ اقالہ کرنے کے بعد اگر بائع نے مشتری سے مبیع واپس نہیں لی بلکہ وہ مبیع اسی مشتری کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دی تو یہ بیع جائز ہے اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اقالہ عاقدین کے حق میں فسخ بیع ہے کیونکہ اگر اقالہ عاقدین کے حق میں بیع ہوتا تو مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اس کا بیچنا لازم آتا حالانکہ مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مشتری کے لئے اس کا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اور اگر اقالہ کے بعد مبیع پر قبضہ کئے بغیر بائع نے مشتری کے علاوہ دوسرے کسی آدمی کے ہاتھ بیع کی تو یہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عاقدین کے علاوہ کے حق میں اقالہ بیع جدید ہے اور بیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچنا چونکہ جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے بائع کا (جو اقالہ میں مشتری ہے) مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچنا جائز نہ ہوگا اور اقالہ، غیر عاقدین کے حق میں بیع جدید ہے اس کا فائدہ اس مثال میں ظاہر ہو گا کہ ایک آدمی نے مکان خریدا پھر شفیع نے حق شفعہ کا دعوی نہ کر کے اپنا حق چھوڑ دیا پھر عاقدین نے اقالہ کیا اور مکان بائع کی ملک میں آگیا تو وہی شفیع اگر شفعہ کا مطالبہ کرنا چاہے تو اس کو یہ اختیار ہے یعنی شفیع شفعہ طلب کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ شفیع کے حق میں اقالہ بیع جدید ہے گویا مشتری نے بائع کو وہی مکان فروخت کر دیا ہے جو اس سے
[PAGE_246] 245 Kitab al-Buyu'. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 8. Evidence... There is a hadith, the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'Whoever rescinds the sale of a regretful person, Allah will remove his stumbles on the Day of Resurrection.' That is, if a person after selling regrets and shows intention to rescind, and the other contracting party rescinds the sale (i.e., annuls the sale), then Allah will remove the lapses of that last contracting party on the Day of Resurrection. So, the Prophet (PBUH) informed of reward or prayed for reward upon doing iqalah, and both are attached to a legislated matter, not an unlegislated one. Thus it is proven that iqalah is legislated. The second evidence is that iqalah is the name of terminating the contract, and the contract is the right of the contracting parties, because it was concluded by their mutual consent. So since the contract is their right and was concluded by their consent, they have full authority to revoke it when necessary. 

'If he stipulates more or less than it, the condition is void, and he returns a price equal to the first price. The principle is that iqalah is a rescission (faskh) regarding the contracting parties and a new sale regarding others, unless it is impossible to make it a rescission, then it becomes void.' This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, it is a sale, unless it is impossible to make it a sale, then it is made a rescission, unless impossible, then it becomes void. According to Muhammad, it is a rescission, unless it is impossible to make it a rescission, then it is made a sale, unless impossible, then it becomes void. Muhammad's evidence is that the word 'iqalah' in language means annulment and removal; hence it is said 'forgive my stumble' and his affair is forgiven him. When that is impossible, it is carried to its probable meaning, which is sale. Do you not see that it is a sale regarding a third party? Abu Yusuf's evidence is that it is an exchange of property by mutual consent, and this is the definition of sale; therefore it is invalidated by the destruction of the commodity, and it is returned due to defect, and preemption is established by it, and these are rulings of a sale. Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the word indicates annulment and removal as we said, and the principle is to apply words according to their real implications. The word 'iqalah' does not bear the meaning of initiating a contract to be carried upon it when annulment is impossible, because it is its opposite, and a word does not bear its opposite. So voidness is determined. And its being a sale regarding a third party is a necessary matter because by it a ruling similar to sale is established, namely ownership, not because of the expression of iqalah, since they have no authority over others. 

Translation: So if he stipulates more than the first price or less, the condition is void and the seller returns the like of the first price. The principle is that iqalah is a rescission regarding the contracting parties and a new sale regarding others. But if it is not possible to make it a rescission, then iqalah will be void. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, iqalah is a sale, but if it is not possible to make it a sale, then it will be made a rescission, but if it is not possible to make it a rescission, then iqalah becomes void. According to Imam Muhammad, iqalah is a rescission, but when it is impossible to make it a rescission, it will be made a sale, but if it is not possible to make it a sale, then iqalah becomes void. Imam Muhammad's evidence is that the word 'iqalah' in language means annulment and removal; hence it is said 'forgive my stumble'. So the word 'iqalah' will be given its full meaning that the word requires. When this meaning is impossible, iqalah is carried upon its probable meaning, which is sale. Do you not see that iqalah is a new sale regarding a third party? Abu Yusuf's evidence is that iqalah is an exchange of property by mutual consent, and this is the definition of sale. For this reason, iqalah is invalidated by the destruction of the commodity, and it is returned due to defect, and preemption is established by iqalah, whereas all these are rulings of a sale. And Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the word 'iqalah' informs of annulment and removal as we said, and the principle is that words are applied according to their real meanings. The word 'iqalah' does not bear the meaning of initiating a contract to be carried upon it when annulment is impossible, because a sale contract is the opposite of annulment, and a word does not bear its opposite. So voidness is determined. And iqalah's being a sale regarding a third party is a necessary matter because by iqalah a ruling similar to sale is established, namely ownership, not because of the expression of iqalah, since the seller and buyer have no authority over others. 

Explanation of the case: If in iqalah a condition of more than the first price or less is stipulated, then this condition is void, and the seller must return the first price. For example, something was sold for one thousand rupees, and the seller took possession of the price and the buyer took possession of the commodity. Now if iqalah is to be done, the seller must return one thousand rupees. Stipulating more or less than one thousand rupees is not valid. So if the seller stipulates to give two hundred rupees less, or the buyer stipulates to take two hundred rupees more, this condition is void, and the seller is only required to return one thousand rupees. 

Imam Abu Hanifa's position: The author of Hidaya said that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, iqalah regarding the two contracting parties is a rescission of the sale, and regarding others it is a new sale. The benefit of it being a rescission regarding the two contracting parties is that the seller is only required to return the price, and the condition of more or less is void. If iqalah were a sale regarding them, then whatever they specified, whether more or less than the first price, would be obligatory, because in a sale the price that the parties specify is what becomes obligatory, not anything else. Thus, the obligation of returning only the first price, and not the specified amount, is evidence that iqalah regarding the parties is a rescission, not a new sale. The second benefit is that iqalah is not invalidated by invalid conditions. If iqalah were a sale regarding them, invalid conditions would invalidate it, just as a sale is invalidated by invalid conditions. So iqalah not being invalidated by invalid conditions is evidence that iqalah regarding the parties is a rescission, not a sale. The third benefit is that after iqalah, if the seller does not take back the commodity from the buyer but sells the same commodity to that same buyer, this sale is valid. This also indicates that iqalah regarding the parties is a rescission, because if iqalah were a sale regarding them, selling before taking possession would be necessary, whereas selling the commodity before taking possession is not permissible for the buyer. And if after iqalah, without taking possession of the commodity, the seller sells it to someone other than the buyer, this is not permissible. Because regarding others, iqalah is a new sale, and selling before taking possession is not permissible, so the seller (who is the buyer in the iqalah) selling before taking possession is not permissible. And iqalah regarding non-parties is a new sale. Its benefit appears in this example: A man bought a house, then the neighbor with preemption waived his right without claiming it. Then the parties did iqalah, and the house came into the seller's ownership. Now if that (original) neighbor (shafi') wants to claim preemption, he has that right, because regarding the shafi', iqalah is a new sale, as if the buyer sold that same house to the seller.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal nature of iqalah (rescission of a sale). It first establishes the validity of iqalah using a hadith and rational reasoning, then presents the ruling when a different price is stipulated in iqalah, and finally details the differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. 

The hadith cited is a well-known one: 'Whoever rescinds the sale of a regretful person, Allah will remove his stumbles on the Day of Resurrection.' This proves that iqalah is mashru' (legislated). Additionally, since the contract is the right of the parties, they have the authority to terminate it by mutual agreement.

The core ruling is: If in iqalah a condition is made to return more or less than the original price, the condition is void and only the original price must be returned. This is based on the principle that iqalah is a rescission (faskh) between the original parties, not a new sale. The passage then explains the positions of the three imams:
- Abu Hanifa holds that iqalah is a rescission regarding the parties, and if it cannot be a rescission (due to impossibility), it becomes void. It is treated as a new sale only regarding third parties out of necessity.
- Abu Yusuf holds that iqalah is essentially a new sale (bay'), and only if it cannot be a sale is it treated as a rescission.
- Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that iqalah is essentially a rescission, but if that is impossible, it is treated as a new sale.

The passage then elaborates on the practical consequences: because iqalah is a rescission between the parties, only the original price is due (not any stipulated amount), invalid conditions do not void the iqalah, and the seller can immediately resell the commodity to the same buyer without needing to take possession. Regarding third parties (e.g., a preemptor), iqalah is treated as a new sale, so the preemptor can claim preemption even after the original parties have rescinded.

The commentary emphasizes that despite this disagreement on the nature, the ruling on the voidness of a price condition is agreed upon, and the typical Hanafi practice follows the principle that iqalah is faskh.

Key Terms
اقالة (iqālah): Rescission of a sale by mutual agreement of the parties after the contract is concluded.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of a contract, treating it as if it never existed, here specifically for the original contracting parties.
بيع (bay‘): A sale; here used as a new contract with all its rulings, as opposed to rescission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a practical consequence of treating iqalah as a new sale (bay')?
A) The original price must be returned regardless of stipulation.
B) Preemption (shuf'ah) is established for a neighbor.
C) The seller can resell to the same buyer without taking possession.
D) Invalid conditions do not void the iqalah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether iqalah is faskh or bay', but the ruling on the price condition is agreed; the difference affects preemption and the effect of invalid conditions.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Iqalah: Faskh or Bay'? The Three Hanafi Positions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Iqalah's legal nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad on the legal nature of Iqalah, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) in cases such as the birth of a child or change of price.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: faskh for parties, new sale for others; Abu Yusuf: sale first; Muhammad: faskh first.

Iqalah is the mutual rescission of a sale. The Hanafi school has a famous three-imam dispute on whether it operates as a rescission of the original contract or a new sale. This lesson lays out each imam's default position and the order of resort when that default fails.

Guided Path
1
Define Iqalah and the legal issue
State what Iqalah is and why its legal nature matters.
2
Identify each imam's default
Abu Hanifa: faskh for parties, bay' for others. Abu Yusuf: bay' primarily. Muhammad: faskh primarily.
Note the hierarchical priority for each.
3
Apply to examples
Work through the examples: slave girl with child, sale before possession, change of price.
See how each imam's view changes the outcome.
4
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the school is Abu Hanifa's.

اور اگر اس باندی نے بچہ جنا تو اس کو فسخ قرار دینا ممکن نہ ہوگا کیونکہ زیادتی منفصلہ فسخ بیع کو روکتی ہے پس جب اس صورت میں فسخ ممکن نہیں تو اس کو بیع قرار دیا جائے گا یعنی یہ کہا جائے گا کہ مشتری نے باندی اور بچہ دونوں کو ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض بائع کے ہاتھ فروخت کیا ہے اور اگر کسی نے ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض باندی خریدی اور مشتری نے قبضہ کئے بغیر ہی دس من گندم پر اقالہ کیا تو یہ اقالہ نہ فسخ بیع ہوسکتا ہے اور نہ بیع ہوسکتا ہے فسخ بیع تو اس لئے نہیں ہو سکتا کہ فسخ ثمن اول پر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ ثمن اول کی جنس کے خلاف پر حالانکہ یہاں ثمن اول کی جنس کے خلاف پر اقالہ کیا گیا ہے اور بیع اس لئے نہیں ہو سکتا کہ قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیع جائز نہیں ہوتی حالانکہ یہاں مشتری نے مبیع یعنی باندی پر قبضہ کئے بغیر ہی اقالہ کیا ہے پس جب نہ فسخ ممکن ہے اور نہ بیع ممکن ہے تو اقالہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور جب اقالہ باطل ہے تو عقد اول اپنے حال پر باقی رہے گا۔
امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقالہ کے لغوی معنی فسخ کرنے اور دور کرنے کے ہیں چنانچہ دعا کے موقع پر کہا جاتا ہے اقلنی عثرتی میری لغزش کو دور کر دے اور اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں تحریر ہے کہ جب تک حقیقت پر عمل کرنا ممکن ہو تو مجاز کی طرف رجوع نہیں کیا جاتا اسلئے لفظ اقالہ کو حقیقی معنی پر محمول کرتے ہوئے کہا گیا کہ اقالہ فسخ بیع ہے۔ اور جب حقیقی معنی یعنی فسخ پر محمول کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو اس کے محتمل
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume eight. Iqalah becomes invalid and the sale is returned due to defect, and the right of pre-emption is established due to Iqalah, though these are all rulings of sale. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the word Iqalah indicates revocation and removal, as we have said, and the principle is that words are to be acted upon in their real meanings, and the word Iqalah does not carry the possibility of initiating a contract so that at the time of revocation it could be interpreted as a new contract. Because a contract of sale is the opposite of revocation, and a word does not carry the possibility of its opposite, so it becomes necessarily invalid. And Iqalah being a sale with respect to a third party is a necessary matter because by Iqalah ownership is established like in a sale, not by the requirement of the verbal formula. It is a sale because the seller and buyer do not have authority over others. Explanation of the case: if in Iqalah a condition of more or less than the first price is stipulated, that condition is void and the seller must return the first price. For example, something was sold for one thousand rupees, and the seller took possession of the price and the buyer took possession of the sold item. Now if they want to make an Iqalah, the seller must return one thousand rupees; it is not valid to stipulate more or less. Thus, if the seller stipulates to give two hundred rupees less, or the buyer stipulates to take two hundred rupees more, this condition is void, and the seller must only return one thousand rupees. The doctrine of Imam Abu Hanifa: The author of Hidayah stated that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Iqalah is a rescission (faskh) of the sale with respect to the contracting parties and a new sale with respect to others. The benefit of it being rescission with respect to the contracting parties is that the seller is only obliged to return the price, and any condition of more or less is void. If Iqalah were a sale for them, whatever they fixed, whether more or less than the first price, would be obligatory because in a sale the price fixed by the parties is what becomes obligatory, not anything else. So the fact that in Iqalah the seller must return the first price and not the fixed condition proves that Iqalah is rescission, not a new sale. Second benefit: Iqalah is not invalidated by void conditions. If it were a sale, it would be invalidated by void conditions, just as a sale is invalidated by void conditions. So the fact that Iqalah is not invalidated by void conditions proves it is rescission, not a sale. Third benefit: after making Iqalah, if the seller does not take back the sold item but sells it to the same buyer, this sale is valid. This also shows Iqalah is rescission for the parties because if it were a sale, selling before taking possession would be required, but selling before possession is not permissible for the buyer. If after Iqalah, without taking possession of the sold item, the seller sells it to someone other than the buyer, it is not valid. Because for others, Iqalah is a new sale, and selling before taking possession of the sold item is not permissible. So the seller (who is the buyer in the Iqalah) cannot sell before taking possession. And Iqalah being a new sale for non-contracting parties is evident in this example: a person bought a house, then the pre-emptor did not claim his right and abandoned it. Then the contracting parties made an Iqalah, and the house came into the seller's ownership. The same pre-emptor, if he wants to claim pre-emption, he has the right; he can demand pre-emption because for him Iqalah is a new sale, as if the buyer sold the same house back to the seller. And in the case of sale, the pre-emptor has the right of pre-emption, so in Iqalah also he has the right. In any case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Iqalah is rescission for the parties and a new sale for others. But if it is not possible to consider Iqalah as rescission, then Iqalah becomes invalid. For example, a person sold a slave girl, and the buyer took possession, then she gave birth to a child. If the parties now want to make an Iqalah, it is not valid. Because Iqalah for them is rescission, and an increase in the sold item that is separate from it prevents rescission. So the separate increase, i.e., the child, legally prevents rescission. When rescission is not possible due to the child, Iqalah becomes invalid, and the original sale remains as it was. The doctrine of Imam Abu Yusuf: According to Imam Abu Yusuf, Iqalah is a sale. But if it is not possible to consider it a sale, then it is considered rescission. And if it is not possible to consider it rescission either, then Iqalah becomes invalid. For example, a person bought a slave for one thousand rupees, the buyer took possession, then they made an Iqalah. This Iqalah is a sale, i.e., the buyer sold the same slave back to the seller for one thousand rupees. If the buyer made an Iqalah before taking possession, then it is not possible to consider it a sale because selling a movable thing before taking possession is not permissible. If someone bought a slave for one thousand rupees and made an Iqalah for ten maunds of wheat before taking possession, this Iqalah cannot be considered a sale because the buyer made an Iqalah without taking possession, and it cannot be considered rescission because rescission is for the first price, while here they made the price ten maunds of wheat, and rescission is not done for something different from the first price. So when neither sale nor rescission is possible, then the Iqalah itself becomes invalid, and the original contract remains. The doctrine of Imam Muhammad: According to Imam Muhammad, Iqalah is rescission. If rescission is not possible, then it is considered a sale. And if sale is also not possible, then Iqalah becomes invalid. For example, a person bought a slave girl for one thousand rupees and took possession, then made an Iqalah for one thousand rupees. This Iqalah is rescission. If the slave girl gave birth to a child, then rescission is not possible because a separate increase prevents rescission. So when rescission is not possible, it is considered a sale, i.e., it is said that the buyer sold both the slave girl and the child to the seller for one thousand rupees. If someone bought a slave girl for one thousand rupees and made an Iqalah for ten maunds of wheat before taking possession, then this Iqalah can neither be rescission nor sale. It cannot be rescission because rescission is for the first price, not for something different from the first price, and here the Iqalah is made for something different from the first price. It cannot be sale because selling before taking possession is not permissible. So when neither rescission nor sale is possible, the Iqalah becomes invalid, and the original contract remains. The proof of Imam Muhammad: The literal meaning of Iqalah is to revoke and remove. Thus, in supplication it is said: 'Aqilni 'athrati (remove my slip). And in books of usul al-fiqh it is written that as long as acting upon the real meaning is possible, one does not resort to the metaphorical. Therefore, the word Iqalah is interpreted in its real meaning, so it is said that Iqalah is rescission. And when it is not possible to interpret it in its real meaning, i.e., rescission, then resort to its possible metaphorical meaning.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) among the three senior imams of the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the legal nature of Iqalah (rescission of a contract by mutual consent). The core question is whether Iqalah operates as a rescission (faskh) of the original sale or as a new sale (bay' jadid). The author first presents the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, then that of Imam Abu Yusuf, and finally that of Imam Muhammad, along with their respective proofs and examples. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that Iqalah is faskh for the contracting parties themselves but a new sale for third parties (such as a pre-emptor). He gives three benefits (fawa'id) to support this: (1) only the original price must be returned, not any extra amount stipulated; (2) void conditions do not invalidate it; (3) if the seller subsequently sells the item to the same buyer without taking possession, it is valid. Imam Abu Yusuf considers Iqalah essentially a sale, but if that is impossible, it becomes faskh; if neither is possible, it is void. Imam Muhammad considers it essentially faskh, but if that is impossible, it becomes a sale; if neither works, it is void. Each imam provides examples to illustrate their views: the case of a slave girl giving birth, the case of selling before possession, and the case of changing the price (thaman) to a different type. The passage ends with Imam Muhammad's proof from the literal meaning of the word 'Iqalah' and the usul principle that the real meaning is prioritized. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each imam's view and the reasoning behind it. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school is generally that of Imam Abu Hanifa, though this is not explicitly stated in this passage.

Key Terms
إقالة (Iqalah): Mutual rescission of a contract of sale by the contracting parties, returning the sold item and price.
فسخ (Faskh): Annulment or rescission of a contract, returning it to its original state before the contract.
بيع جديد (Bay' Jadid): A new sale contract, as if the buyer sells the item back to the seller for a new price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a sold slave girl gives birth to a child after the buyer takes possession, and then the parties wish to make an Iqalah, what is the ruling?
A) The Iqalah is valid as a rescission because the child is part of the mother.
B) The Iqalah is invalid because the child is a separate increase that prevents rescission.
C) The Iqalah is valid as a new sale of both mother and child.
D) The Iqalah is considered a sale of the mother only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes Iqalah as fundamentally a rescission for the parties, though the imams differ on the hierarchy of faskh and bay'.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Abu Hanifa's Proofs for Iqalah as Faskh
Detailed proofs of Abu Hanifa's position on Iqalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three benefits (fawa'id) that Abu Hanifa uses to prove that Iqalah is faskh for the parties, and evaluate the strength of his linguistic and practical arguments.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's three benefits: no price change, void conditions don't invalidate, and same-buyer sale without possession is valid.

Imam Abu Hanifa provides three practical benefits to support his view that Iqalah is a rescission for the contracting parties. Each benefit demonstrates that the legal consequences of Iqalah align with faskh, not bay'. This lesson examines those arguments in detail.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic argument
The word iqalah means revocation, not initiation.
2
First benefit: only first price returned
If it were a sale, any new price would replace the first; here the first price is returned.
3
Second benefit: void conditions harmless
In a sale, void conditions invalidate; here they don't.
4
Third benefit: same buyer sale without possession
If it were a sale, pre-possession sale is invalid; here it is valid.
5
Understand the third-party perspective
For others (e.g., pre-emptor), it is a new sale.
