اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہشتم
قرار دینا ممکن نہ ہو تو ا قالہ باطل ہو جائے گا تو اس ضابطہ کی روشنی میں ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جب شمن اول سے زیادہ کی شرط مثلا لگائی مثلا من اول ایک ہزار روپے ہیں مگر بائع اور مشتری نے اقالہ پندرہ سو روپے پر کیا یعنی مشتری نے یہ شیرا لگائی کہ بائع بجائے ایک ہزار روپے کے پندرہ سوروپے واپس کرے گا اور بائع نے اس کو منظور کر لیا تو اقالہ ایک ہزار روپے کے عوض میں ہو جائے گا اور باقی پانچ سو روپے کا ذکر اغو ہو جائے گا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثمن اول سے زائد پر بیع کو فتح کرنا ناممکن ہے کیونکہ منبج بیع نام ہے۔ بیع کو دو کرنا اس وصف پر جس پر وہ پہلے سے تھی اور شمن اول سے زائد پر فسخ کرنا ایسا نہیں ہے کیونکہ ثمن اول سے زائد پر مسح کرنے میں اس چیز کو دور رنا لازم آتا ہے جو ثابت نہیں تھی یعنی پندرہ سو روپے پر مسح کرنے کی صورت میں پانچ سوروپے جو عقد بیع میں ثابت نہیں تھے ان کو دور کرنا لازم آتا ہے اور جو چیز ثابت نہ ہواس کو دور کرنا محال ہے۔ اسلئے شمن اول سے زائد کی شرط لگانا باطل ہو جائیگا لیکن اقالہ باطل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اقالہ شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتا کہ زیادتی کی شرط ربوا کے مشابہ ہو گئی اور ا قالہ معنی کے اعتبار سے بیچ کے مشابہ ہے پس اقالہ کے اندر شرط فاسد شبیہ الشبیہ ہوگئی اور پہلے گذر چکا کہ شبہۃ الر ہوا تو مؤثر نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس شرط سے اقالہ درست ہو جائے گا مگر یہ شرط خود باطل ہو جائے گی۔ برخلاف بیچ کے یعنی فتح تو زیادتی پر متعدد ہے لیکن بیچ زیادتی پر متعد نہیں ہے مثلاً ایک آدمی نے ایک درہم دو درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا تو یہ بیچ درہم زائدہ کے ثابت ہونے سے باطل ہے اور یہ نہیں کہا جاسکتا کہ ایک درہم کو ایک درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا اور درہم زائد باطل ہو گیا کیونکہ بیچ کے اندر درہم زائد کا ثابت کرناممکن ہے اور جب درہم زائد کا ثابت کرنا ممکن ہے تو ربو متحقق ہو گیا اور ر بوا کی وجہ سے بیع باطل ہو جاتی ہے اس لیے درہم زائد کی وجہ سے بیع باطل ہو جائے گی لیکن اقالہ کے اندر زیادتی کا ثابت کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے کیونکہ اقالہ نام ہے ثابت شدہ چیز کو دور کرنے کا اور زیادتی جو بیع کے اندر ثابت نہیں تھی اس کو دور کرنا محال ہے اس لیے اقالہ کے اندر زیادتی کی شرط باطل ہو جائے گی لیکن اقالہ باطل نہیں ہوگا۔
اسی طرح اگر شمن اول سے کم کی شرط لگائی ہو مثلا شمن اول ایک ہزار روپیہ ہے اور اقالہ کرتے وقت بائع نے کہا کہ میں آٹھ سو روپیہ واپس کروں گا تو یہ شرط باطل ہو جائے گی اور ثمن اول یعنی ایک ہزار روپیہ پر ا قالہ درست ہو جائے گا کیونکہ غیر ثابت شدہ چیز کو دور کرنا۔ محال ہے اور بیچ کے اندر نقصان ثمن اول سے کمی کی شرط بھی ثابت نہیں تھی لہذا اقالہ کے ذریعہ اس کو دور کرنا محال ہوگا اور جب یہ محال ہے تو شرط باطل اور اقالہ صحیح ہو جائے گا ہاں اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مبیع کے اندر کوئی عیب پیدا ہو گیا تو ایسی صورت میں ثمن اول سے کم پر بھی اقالہ جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ ثمن اول میں سے جو مقدار کم کی گئی ہے مثلاً دو سور و پیہ تو یہ دو سو روپیہ بیع کے اس جز کے مقابل قرار دیے جائیں گے جو جز مشتری کے قبضہ میں فوت ہو گیا ہے یعنی عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع کا جو جز مشتری کے پاس رہ گیا ہے بائع نے اس کے مقابلہ میں شمن کی ایک مقدار یعنی دوسور و پیر کو روک لیا ہے اور اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے امام صاحب کے مذہب کا حاصل یہ ہوا کہ اگر ایک غلام ایک ہزار ردو پہیہ میں خریدا اور ایک ہزار روپیہ پر اقالہ کیا تو اقالہ درست ہے۔ اور اگر پندرہ سو روپیہ پرا قالہ کیا تو ایک ہزار روپیہ پر ا قالہ صحیح ہے اور پانچ سوروپیہ کی شرط باطل ہے اور اگر نو سو روپیہ پرا قالہ کیا اور مبیع کے اندر کوئی عیب بھی پیدا نہیں ہوا تو اقالہ ایک ہزار روپیہ پر سیح۔ نقصان کی شرط باطل ہے اور اگر طبیع کے اندر عیب پیدا ہو گیا تو ایسی صورت میں مقدار مشروط یعنی نو سور و پیہ پر ہی اقالہ صحیح : دجائے گا۔

تو صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ اقالہ، بیج ہو گا اور یہ کہا جائے گا کہ مشتری نے جو مبیع ایک ہزار روپیہ میں خریدی تھی ، بائع کو پندرہ سو روپیہ میں فروخت کر دی ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تو اقالہ کا بیچ ہونا ہی اصل ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اصل تو اقالہ نیخ ہونا ہے مگر چونکہ زیادتی کی شرط پر فسح متعذر ہے اور ا قالہ کو اگر فسخ قرار دینا ممکن نہ ہو تو اس کو بیع قرار دیا جاتا ہے اس لیے ان کے نزدیک بھی یہا قالہ بیج ہوگا پس جب شمن اول پر زیادتی کی شرط لگائی تو چونکہ حقیقت یعنی فتح پر عمل متعد ر ہو گیا۔ اس لئے عقلاء کے کلام کولغو ہونے سے بچانے کے لیے مجاز یعنی بیچ کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا اور یہ کہا جائے گا کہ اس کلام سے عاقدین کا مقصد بیع کرنا ہے نہ کہ صبح بیچ کرنا۔ اور اگر شمن اول سے کم کی شرط لگائی مثلاً بائع نے کہا کہ بجائے ایک ہزار روپیہ کے آٹھ سو روپیہ واپس کروں گا اور مشتری نے اس کو منظور کر لیا تو حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقالہ کا بیچ ہونا ہی اصل ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک یہ اقالہ بہمن اول پر فسخ ہے یعنی بائع پر شمن اول یعنی ایک ہزار روپیہ واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا اور کمی کی شرط لگانا باطل ہوگا ۔
امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب بائع نے یہ کہا کہ میں آٹھ سو روپیہ واپس کروں گا تو اس سے ثمن اول کے ایک حصہ سے سکوت اختیار کیا اور اگر وہ پورے شن کے ذکر سے سکوت کرتا اور اقالہ کر لیتا تو یہ پورے شمن پر فتح ہوتا پس جب شمن اول کے ایک حصہ سے سکوت کیا تو یہ ا قالہ بدرجہ اولی فسخ ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ شمن اول سے کم پر اقالہ کرنے کی صورت میں فسخ چونکہ ممکن ہے اس لیے امام محمد کے نزدیک اس صورت میں اقالہ مسخ ہوگا اور ثمن اول سے زائد پرا قالہ کرنے کی صورت میں چونکہ فتح ممکن نہیں ہے اس لیے اس صورت میں امام محمد کے نزدیک اقالہ، بیج ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مبیع کے اندر عیب پیدا ہو گیا تو شمن اول سے کم پر ہی اقالہ فسخ ہوگا یعنی مقدار مشروط یعنی آٹھ سوروپیہ ہی بائع پر واجب ہوں گے ایک ہزار روپیہ یعنی پوراشن اول واپس کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے۔
When it is not possible to make (the iqalah) then the iqalah becomes void. In light of this principle, we say: when a condition of more than the first price is made, e.g. first price is one thousand rupees but the seller and buyer made iqalah for fifteen hundred rupees, i.e. the buyer stipulated that the seller will return fifteen hundred instead of one thousand, and the seller agreed, then the iqalah will be in exchange for one thousand rupees, and the mention of the remaining five hundred rupees becomes void. The proof is that rescinding the sale for more than the first price is impossible, because rescission means annulling the contract as it was. To rescind for more than the first price requires removing something that was not established, i.e. five hundred rupees that were not established in the contract. Removing something not established is impossible. Therefore, the condition of more than the first price is void, but the iqalah does not become void because iqalah is not invalidated by a corrupt condition. The condition of excess resembles riba, and iqalah resembles sale in meaning. Thus, a corrupt condition in iqalah is a likeness of a likeness (shabih al-shabih), and it was previously stated that mere resemblance to riba is not effective. Hence, the iqalah becomes valid, but the condition becomes void. Contrary to sale: rescission on excess is impossible, but sale on excess is not impossible. For example, if a man sold one dirham for two dirhams, this sale is void due to the establishment of the extra dirham. It cannot be said that he sold one dirham for one dirham and the extra dirham is void, because in sale it is possible to establish the extra dirham. When it is possible, riba is established and the sale becomes void due to riba. In iqalah, establishing the excess is not possible because iqalah means removing something already established, and the excess was not established in the sale, so removing it is impossible. Therefore, the condition of excess in iqalah is void, but the iqalah itself is not void. Similarly, if a condition of less than the first price is made, e.g. first price is one thousand rupees, and at the time of iqalah the seller said 'I will return eight hundred rupees', then this condition is void and the iqalah is valid on the first price of one thousand rupees, because removing something unestablished is impossible. The deficiency was not established in the sale, so removing it via iqalah is impossible. When it is impossible, the condition is void and the iqalah is valid. However, if a defect occurred in the sold item in the buyer's possession, then in such a case iqalah at less than the first price is permissible, because the amount reduced is offset against the part of the sold item that was lost in the buyer's possession. The gist of Imam (Abu Hanifa)'s madhhab: if a slave is purchased for one thousand rupees and iqalah is made for one thousand rupees, the iqalah is valid. If iqalah is for fifteen hundred rupees, the iqalah is valid for one thousand rupees and the condition of five hundred is void. If iqalah is for nine hundred rupees and no defect occurred, the iqalah is valid for one thousand rupees and the condition of deficiency is void. If a defect occurred, then iqalah is valid for the stipulated amount of nine hundred rupees. According to the Sahibayn, in the case of increase, this iqalah is a sale. The buyer, who bought for one thousand, is deemed to have sold to the seller for fifteen hundred. The proof: Abu Yusuf's principle is that iqalah is fundamentally a sale. Muhammad's principle is that iqalah is fundamentally a rescission, but when rescission is impossible due to the condition of excess, the iqalah is treated as a sale. So in the case of increase, since the literal meaning (rescission) cannot apply, they resort to the metaphorical meaning (sale) to avoid making the parties' speech void. In the case of a condition of less than the first price, according to Abu Yusuf, iqalah is fundamentally a sale; according to Muhammad, it is a rescission on the first price, and the condition of deficiency is void. Muhammad's proof: when the seller said 'I will return eight hundred', he remained silent about a part of the first price. If he had remained silent about the entire first price and performed iqalah, it would be a rescission on the full price. So when he remained silent about a part, the iqalah is a rescission by stronger reason. Summary: In the case of lower price, rescission is possible, so Muhammad holds it as rescission; in the case of higher price, rescission is impossible, so he holds it as a sale. Sahib al-Hidayah says: if a defect occurred in the buyer's possession, then iqalah at less than the first price is a rescission for the stipulated amount, not for the full first price. The proof has passed earlier.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale) when the parties agree on a different price than the original. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The commentary first presents the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: if the agreed price is higher than the original, the condition of increase is void, but the iqalah is valid on the original price. The reasoning is that iqalah is a rescission, and rescission can only remove what was established in the contract; the extra amount was never established, so it cannot be removed, making the condition impossible. Therefore, the condition is void, but the iqalah itself remains valid because iqalah is not invalidated by a corrupt condition that is similar to a likeness (shabih al-shabih). In contrast, in a sale, such an increase would establish riba and void the entire contract because the extra amount can be established. If the agreed price is lower than the original, the same principle applies: the condition of deficiency is void, and iqalah is on the original price, unless a defect occurred in the sold item in the buyer's possession, in which case the reduction is considered compensation for the defect, and the iqalah is valid on the reduced amount. Then the passage presents the views of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). For a higher price, both Sahibayn consider the iqalah as a sale (new contract) because rescission is impossible. For a lower price, Abu Yusuf also considers it a sale, while Muhammad considers it a rescission on the original price with the condition void, because rescission is possible. The commentator also quotes the view of Sahib al-Hidayah confirming that in case of a defect, iqalah at the lower price is a rescission for the stipulated amount.

Key Terms
إقالة (iqālah): Rescission of a sale contract by mutual consent, returning the goods and price to their original owners.
ثمن أول (thaman awwal): The original price agreed upon in the sale contract.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of a contract, returning to the state before the contract.
شرط فاسد (shart fāsid): A corrupt or invalid condition that does not invalidate the contract in iqalah but is itself void.
لغو (laghw): Void, legally ineffective; the mention of the extra amount is considered void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the parties agree to iqalah for a price lower than the original price (e.g., original 1000, iqalah for 800) and no defect occurred, what is the ruling?
A) The iqalah is a sale for 800.
B) The iqalah is valid as a rescission on the original price of 1000, and the condition of 800 is void.
C) The iqalah is void because the condition is invalid.
D) The iqalah is valid for 800 because of the mutual agreement.

Key Takeaway
In iqalah, conditions of higher or lower price are void, and the contract stands on the original price, except when a defect justifies a reduction.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Iqalah with a Different Price Genus
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqalah with different price genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqalah when the price is of a different genus and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Iqalah with different genus: Abu Hanifa sees rescission, Sahibayn see a new sale.

This lesson examines a scenario where parties cancel a sale but with a different type of price (e.g., originally dirhams, now dinars). The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa treats it as rescission on the original price, deeming the mention of the different genus void. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) treat it as a new sale. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing the legal consequences, such as the right to object to defects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed element
The act is iqalah (mutual rescission of sale). The disputed element is that the price offered in the iqalah is of a different genus from the original price (e.g., gold dinars vs silver dirhams).
The contract's original price genus is the benchmark.
2
State Abu Hanifa’s position
Abu Hanifa holds that the iqalah is a rescission (faskh) with the original price, and the mention of the different genus is void (laghw). The contract is effectively reverted as if the new price was never mentioned.
This is based on the principle that iqalah is fundamentally a rescission, not a sale.
3
State the Sahibayn’s position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the iqalah is a new sale (bay‘). Because the subject matter (price) has changed, rescission of the original contract is impossible, so it must be a fresh transaction.
They analogize it to when a new subject is introduced.
4
Identify the underlying usul principle
The dispute hinges on whether iqalah is always rescission or can be treated as a sale when elements change. Abu Hanifa insists on rescission, while Sahibayn apply the maxim that when rescission is impossible, the transaction becomes a sale.
No explicit rebuttal is given in the text, but each view relies on the nature of iqalah.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If rescission, ownership reverts as before, and the buyer loses the right to claim defects (since it’s not a new sale). If sale, the buyer retains the right to inspect and claim defects, and the contract is subject to all sale rules.
This difference affects the parties' legal positions.

ولو اقال بغير جنس الثمن الأول فهو فسخ بالثمن الأول عند ابي حنيفة ويجعل التسمية لغوا وعندهما بيع لما بينا ولو ولدت المبيعة ولدا ثم تقايلا فالا قالة باطلة عنده لان الولد مانع من الفسخ وعندهما يكون بيعا والاقالة قبل القبض فى المنقول وغيره فسخ عند ابي حنيفة و محمد وكذا عند ابي يوسف في المنقول لتعذر البيع وفى العقار يكون بيعا عنده لا مكان البيع فان بيع العقار قبل القبض جائز عنده

ترجمہ اور اگر شمن اول کے سوا دوسری جنس پر قال کیا تو ہم ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ ثمن اول پر فسخ ہوگا اور شمن اول کی جنس کے علاوہ کا ذکر اغو قرار دیا جائے گا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ قالہ بیچ ہو گا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے اور اگر مبیعہ باندی نے بچہ جنا پھر دونوں نے اقالہ کیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک اقالہ باطل ہے کیونکہ بچہ مانع ضح ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بیج ہوگا اور مقتول کے اندر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اقالہ طرفین کے نزدیک فسخ ہے اور اسی طرح ابو یوسف کے نزدیک منقول میں ( نسخ ہے ) کیونکہ بیع متعد ر ہے اور غیر منقول میں ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقالہ بیع ہے کیونکہ بیع متعذر ہے۔ اور غیر منقول میں ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقالہ بیع ہے کیونکہ بیع ممکن
The ruling of iqalah with other than the genus of the first price: If he makes iqalah with other than the genus of the first price, then according to Abu Hanifa it is a rescission with the first price, and the mention (of the different genus) is considered void. According to them (the Sahibayn), it is a sale, for the reason we have stated. If the sold female slave gives birth to a child, then the two parties make iqalah, then the iqalah is void according to him (Abu Hanifa) because the child prevents rescission. According to them, it is a sale. And the iqalah before possession in movables and other things is a rescission according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and likewise according to Abu Yusuf in movables because sale is not possible, but in immovables it is a sale according to him because sale is possible, for selling immovables before possession is valid according to him. ... Translation: If iqalah is made with a different genus than the first price, then according to Abu Hanifa it is a rescission on the first price, and the mention of the different genus is void. According to the Sahibayn, it is a sale for the reason we have stated. If the sold slave-girl gave birth to a child, then they made iqalah, then according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) the iqalah is void because the child is a prevention of rescission. According to the Sahibayn, it is a sale. And iqalah before possession in movable is rescission according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and similarly according to Abu Yusuf in movables because sale is impossible, and in immovables it is a sale according to him because sale is possible.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage covers three specific rulings on iqalah, each with intra-Hanafi dispute. First, if the iqalah is for a price of a different genus (e.g., original price was dirhams, but iqalah is for dinars), Abu Hanifa holds it as a rescission on the original price, and the mention of the different genus is void. The Sahibayn consider it a sale (new contract). Second, if the sold item is a slave-girl who gives birth before iqalah, then according to Abu Hanifa the child prevents rescission because the sale contract is no longer exactly what it was, so the iqalah is void. The Sahibayn consider it a sale. Third, regarding iqalah before the buyer takes possession: for movables (goods that can be transferred), Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is a rescission; Abu Yusuf also says it is a rescission for movables because a sale before possession is not valid under Hanafi law. For immovables (real estate), Abu Yusuf says the iqalah before possession is a sale because a sale of immovable before possession is valid. The commentary explains each ruling, emphasizing that when rescission is impossible or ineffective, the iqalah is treated as a sale.

Key Terms
جنس الثمن الأول (jins al-thaman al-awwal): The genus or type of the original price (e.g., silver dirhams, gold dinars).
فسخ (faskh): Rescission; the annulment of a contract, causing reversion to pre-contract state.
بيع (bay‘): Sale; a contract transferring ownership in exchange for consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if iqalah is made with a price of a different genus than the original, what is the ruling?
A) The iqalah is void.
B) The iqalah is a rescission with the original price.
C) The iqalah is a new sale.
D) The iqalah is a gift.

Key Takeaway
When the price in iqalah is of a different genus, Abu Hanifa sees rescission while Sahibayn see a new sale; the difference affects defect claims and other sale-related rights.

Iqalah When the Sold Slave-Girl Has Given Birth
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqalah after birth of a child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa considers iqalah void when a sold slave-girl has given birth, and why Sahibayn treat it as a sale.

Core Idea
The child of a sold slave-girl prevents rescission; Abu Hanifa voids iqalah, Sahibayn make it a sale.

This lesson addresses a unique situation: a slave-girl is sold, then gives birth before the parties agree to cancel the sale (iqalah). The child is a new entity not part of the original contract. Abu Hanifa rules that the child prevents rescission, making the iqalah void. The Sahibayn, however, treat the iqalah as a new sale covering both mother and child. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school handles changes in the subject matter before cancellation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the new element
The act is iqalah after the sold slave-girl has given birth. The new element is the child, which was not part of the original sale.
The child is considered separate property owned by the buyer.
2
State Abu Hanifa’s position
Abu Hanifa rules that the iqalah is void (batil) because the child prevents rescission. Rescission would require returning exactly what was sold, but now there is an additional entity (the child) that was not part of the original contract.
The child is a māni‘ (preventer) of rescission.
3
State the Sahibayn’s position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that the iqalah is a sale. Since rescission is not possible, they treat the transaction as a new sale of the mother and child together.
Again, the principle: when rescission is impossible, it becomes a sale.
4
Understand the reasoning behind each view
Abu Hanifa emphasizes the conceptual identity of the sold item; any addition (child) makes rescission impossible, so iqalah fails. Sahibayn focus on the parties' intention to unwind the deal and allow a new sale to effect that intent.
No clear rebuttal is recorded in the passage.
5
Consider the practical consequences
If void, the original sale remains; the buyer keeps the slave-girl and child, and the seller keeps the price. If a sale, the seller buys back the mother and child at an agreed price, and the buyer transfers ownership back.
The parties must be aware of the legal effect to plan accordingly.

Source Text

باطل (bāṭil): Void; a contract that is legally invalid and produces no effects.
بيع (bay‘): Sale; a contract transferring ownership.

D) Because the child belongs to the seller.

Key Takeaway
When a sold slave-girl gives birth before iqalah, Abu Hanifa voids the iqalah due to the child as a barrier, while Sahibayn treat it as a sale.

Iqalah Before Possession: Movables vs Immovables
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqalah before possession for movables and immovables

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on iqalah before possession for movables and immovables, and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Iqalah before possession: for movables it is rescission; for immovables, Abu Yusuf treats it as a sale.

This lesson examines iqalah before the buyer has taken possession of the purchased item. The Hanafi school generally treats iqalah as rescission (faskh) for movables, since a sale before possession is invalid. However, for immovables (real estate), Abu Yusuf holds that iqalah can be a sale because selling immovable before possession is permissible. This distinction highlights how the permissibility of selling before possession influences the nature of iqalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the timing
The act is iqalah before the buyer takes possession (qabd) of the purchased item. The timing is critical because Islamic law restricts selling before possession for movables.
Possession is a key condition in sale contracts.
2
State the general ruling for movables
Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf agree that iqalah before possession in movables (manqul) is a rescission (faskh). Because selling before possession of movables is not valid (sale is impossible), iqalah cannot be a sale.
The impossibility of sale forces it to be rescission.
3
State Abu Yusuf’s ruling for immovables
Abu Yusuf holds that iqalah before possession in immovables (‘iqar) is a sale. This is because selling immovables before possession is valid in Hanafi law, so the iqalah can be a valid sale.
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad would presumably still consider it rescission, but the passage only mentions Abu Yusuf's view.
4
Understand the rationale
The difference stems from the permissibility of selling before possession. For movables, sale is prohibited (based on hadith), so iqalah cannot be a sale; it must be rescission. For immovables, sale is allowed, so iqalah can be structured as a sale.
This is a practical application of the maxim: when sale is impossible, iqalah is rescission; when sale is possible, it can be sale.
5
Consider practical implications
If iqalah is rescission, ownership reverts immediately as if the sale never happened. If it is a sale, the parties enter a new contract with all its conditions (e.g., option of inspection, risk of loss before transfer).
Parties should be aware of their rights and duties.

Source Text

Iqalah with Price Change: Intra-Hanafi Dispute (Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqalah with price changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on iqalah when the stipulated price differs from the original, and apply the correct classification (rescission vs. sale) based on feasibility of rescission.

Core Idea
Iqalah is rescission if possible, sale if not; Abu Yusuf always treats it as sale.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the legal nature of iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale) when the parties agree on a price different from the original. The key question is whether iqalah remains a rescission (faskh) of the original contract or becomes a new sale (bay'). The answer depends on whether the new price is higher or lower and on each Imam's foundational view of iqalah. Understanding this helps in applying the correct legal effects, such as pre-emption rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Locate in the text where the price is increased (e.g., from 1000 to 1500) and where it is decreased (e.g., from 1000 to 800). Note the different treatment.
The text separates increase and decrease cases.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position for each
Abu Yusuf holds that iqalah is always a sale. Therefore, in both increase and decrease, the transaction is a new sale.
His view is based on istihsan (juristic preference).
3
State Muhammad's position for each
Muhammad holds that iqalah is originally rescission, but when rescission is impossible (due to increase or other barrier), it becomes a sale. For decrease, rescission is possible, so it remains rescission; for increase, rescission is impossible, so it becomes a sale.
This is a pragmatic approach based on the feasibility of faskh.
4
Extract the rational proofs (dalil aqli)
For Muhammad: if rescission is impossible (increase), the speech of the contractors must be interpreted as a sale to avoid nullity. If possible (decrease), silence on part of the price indicates partial rescission. For Abu Yusuf: iqalah is inherently a sale, so no conversion is needed.
Both proofs are rational, not based on explicit text.
5
Apply the rule to a defect scenario
The author of al-Hidayah adds: if a defect occurs in the sold item while in buyer's possession, iqalah for a lower price still functions as rescission, requiring return of the reduced amount only.
This confirms that feasibility of rescission is judged at the time of iqalah, not afterwards.

اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم تو صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ اقالہ، بيع ہو گا اور یہ کہا جائے گا کہ مشتری نے جو مبیع ایک ہزار روپیہ میں خریدی تھی، بائع کو پندرہ سو روپیہ میں فروخت کر دی ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تو اقالہ کا بيع ہونا ہی اصل ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اصل تو اقالہ فسخ ہونا ہے مگر چونکہ زیادتی کی شرط پر فسخ متعذر ہے اور اقالہ کو اگر فسخ قرار دینا ممکن نہ ہو تو اس کو بیع قرار دیا جاتا ہے اس لیے ان کے نزدیک بھی یہ اقالہ بيع ہوگا پس جب ثمن اول پر زیادتی کی شرط لگائی تو چونکہ حقیقت یعنی فسخ پر عمل متعذر ہو گیا۔ اس لئے عقلاء کے کلام کو لغو ہونے سے بچانے کے لیے مجاز یعنی بیع کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا اور یہ کہا جائے گا کہ اس کلام سے عاقدین کا مقصد بیع کرنا ہے نہ کہ صرف بیع کرنا۔ اور اگر ثمن اول سے کم کی شرط لگائی مثلاً بائع نے کہا کہ بجائے ایک ہزار روپیہ کے آٹھ سو روپیہ واپس کروں گا اور مشتری نے اس کو منظور کر لیا تو حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقالہ کا بيع ہونا ہی اصل ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک یہ اقالہ بثمن اول پر فسخ ہے یعنی بائع پر ثمن اول یعنی ایک ہزار روپیہ واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا اور کمی کی شرط لگانا باطل ہوگا۔
امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب بائع نے یہ کہا کہ میں آٹھ سو روپیہ واپس کروں گا تو اس سے ثمن اول کے ایک حصہ سے سکوت اختیار کیا اور اگر وہ پورے ثمن کے ذکر سے سکوت کرتا اور اقالہ کر لیتا تو یہ پورے ثمن پر فسخ ہوتا پس جب ثمن اول کے ایک حصہ سے سکوت کیا تو یہ اقالہ بدرجہ اولی فسخ ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ثمن اول سے کم پر اقالہ کرنے کی صورت میں فسخ چونکہ ممکن ہے اس لیے امام محمد کے نزدیک اس صورت میں اقالہ فسخ ہوگا اور ثمن اول سے زائد پر اقالہ کرنے کی صورت میں چونکہ فسخ ممکن نہیں ہے اس لیے اس صورت میں امام محمد کے نزدیک اقالہ، بيع ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مبیع کے اندر عیب پیدا ہو گیا تو ثمن اول سے کم پر ہی اقالہ فسخ ہوگا یعنی مقدار مشروط یعنی آٹھ سو روپیہ ہی بائع پر واجب ہوں گے ایک ہزار روپیہ یعنی پورا ثمن اول واپس کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے۔
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Sharh of Hidayah, Volume 8. According to the Sahibayn, this iqalah will be a sale, and it will be said that the buyer sold the sold item, which he had bought for one thousand rupees, back to the seller for fifteen hundred rupees. The proof is that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, iqalah being a sale is the principle, and according to Imam Muhammad, the principle is that iqalah is a rescission, but because rescission is impossible due to the condition of increase, and if iqalah cannot be considered rescission, it is considered a sale. Therefore, according to him, this iqalah will also be a sale. When the condition of increase over the first price is stipulated, since operation on the reality (i.e., rescission) became impossible, to save the speech of the contractors from being null, recourse is taken to the metaphor (i.e., sale), and it will be said that the intention of the contractors from this speech is a sale, not a rescission. And if the condition of decrease from the first price is stipulated, for example the seller said, 'I will return eight hundred rupees instead of one thousand rupees' and the buyer accepted it, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf, iqalah being a sale is the principle, and according to Imam Muhammad, this iqalah is a rescission based on the first price, i.e., the seller must return the first price (one thousand rupees), and the condition of decrease is void. Imam Muhammad's proof is that when the seller said, 'I will return eight hundred rupees,' he remained silent regarding a portion of the first price. If he had remained silent regarding the entire price and made iqalah, it would have been a rescission of the entire price. So when he remained silent regarding a portion of the first price, this iqalah is a rescission a fortiori. The conclusion is that when iqalah is made for less than the first price, since rescission is possible, according to Imam Muhammad, in this case iqalah is rescission; and when iqalah is made for more than the first price, since rescission is impossible, in this case according to Imam Muhammad iqalah is a sale. The author of al-Hidayah says: If a defect occurs in the sold item while in the buyer's possession, iqalah for less than the first price will still be rescission, i.e., only the stipulated amount (eight hundred rupees) will be obligatory upon the seller, and returning the full first price (one thousand rupees) will not be obligatory. Its proof has passed earlier.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the legal nature of iqalah (rescission of sale) when the parties agree on a different price than the original. The discussion covers two scenarios: increase and decrease. The principle is that iqalah is originally a rescission (فسخ) of the first sale. However, when the parties stipulate a price different from the original, the possibility of rescission varies. If the new price is higher, rescission is impossible because it would effectively be a new sale at a higher price. Thus, both Imams end up treating it as a sale, but for different reasons. Abu Yusuf inherently views iqalah as a sale in any case, while Muhammad applies a general rule: when rescission is impossible, iqalah becomes a sale. If the new price is lower, rescission is possible (by forgiving part of the price), so Muhammad maintains it as rescission, whereas Abu Yusuf still considers it a sale. The passage also includes a comment by the author of al-Hidayah about a defect in the sold item: even if a defect occurs, iqalah for a lower price remains rescission, meaning only the reduced amount is due, not the full original price. This underscores the flexibility of iqalah to accommodate changes while preserving the original contract's rescission where feasible.

Key Terms
اقالة (iqalah): Annulment of a sale by mutual agreement, returning the sold item and price.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission of the original contract, restoring ownership to pre-sale state.
بيع (bay'): Sale; exchange of property for consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the ruling of iqalah when the parties agree on an increased price (e.g., from 1000 to 1500)?
A) It is a rescission (faskh) because iqalah is inherently rescission.
B) It is a sale (bay') because rescission is impossible due to the increase.
C) It is invalid because the price must equal the original.
D) It is a gift because the buyer is paying more.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, iqalah is treated as rescission when feasible; otherwise it becomes a new sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Iqalah with a Different Type of Price
Ruling on iqalah with a different type of price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on iqalah when the price type is changed and explain why Abu Hanifa treats it as rescission while the Sahibayn treat it as a sale.

Core Idea
When the price type changes in iqalah, Abu Hanifa rescinds with the original price; the Sahibayn deem it a new sale.

In commercial transactions, parties may agree to cancel a sale and return the goods for a different price than originally agreed. This lesson examines how the Hanafi school classifies such an iqalah: is it a rescission (faskh) of the original sale or a completely new sale (bay')? The answer depends on the type of price, and the great Imams differ on the legal outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction
Recognize that iqalah is a mutual rescission of a sale, and here the parties agree to use a different currency (e.g., dirhams vs dinars) for the return.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa holds that iqalah is always a rescission; the mention of a different price type is void. The seller must return the original price (e.g., dirhams).
3
State the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that rescission is impossible when the price type changes, so the iqalah becomes a new sale: the buyer sells the item back for the newly specified price.
4
Analyze the reasoning
For Abu Hanifa, iqalah is only rescission; a change in price type does not alter its nature. For the Sahibayn, rescission requires the original terms; if the price changes, the transaction must be a new sale.
5
Identify the practical difference
Under Abu Hanifa, the original sale is annulled and the seller must return the original price. Under the Sahibayn, a new sale occurs, so the buyer (now seller) may be liable for defects, and pre-emption rights may apply.

Ruling of iqalah with a different type than the original price. 'And if he cancels (iqalah) with other than the type of the first price, then it is a rescission based on the first price according to Abu Hanifa, and the naming (of the other type) is considered void. And according to them (Sahibayn), it is a sale, as we have established. And if the sold female slave gives birth to a child, then they make iqalah, the iqalah is void according to him (Abu Hanifa) because the child prevents rescission. And according to them, it would be a sale. And iqalah before delivery, for movable property and other than it, is rescission according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and similarly according to Abu Yusuf for movables, due to the impossibility of sale. And for immovables, according to him, iqalah is a sale because sale is possible, for sale of immovables before delivery is permissible according to him.' Translation: And if iqalah is made with a different type than the first price, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is a rescission based on the first price, and the mention of the other type is considered void. And according to the Sahibayn, this iqalah is a sale due to the proof we mentioned. And if a slave-girl gives birth to a child, then both make iqalah, the iqalah is void according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) because the child prevents rescission. And according to the Sahibayn, it would be a sale. And iqalah before delivery for movables and other things is rescission according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and similarly according to Abu Yusuf for movables because sale is impossible. And for immovables, according to him, iqalah is a sale because sale is possible, for according to Abu Yusuf sale of immovables before delivery is permissible. (Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Sharh of Hidayah, Volume 8) Explanation: The case is that if iqalah is made with a different type than the first price, e.g., the first price was dirhams and iqalah is made with dinars, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this iqalah is a rescission of the sale based on the first price (dirhams), and the mention of dinars is void. That is, the seller must return the first price (dirhams), not the dinars. According to the Sahibayn, this iqalah is a sale with the other type, i.e., it will be said that the buyer sold the item, which he had bought for dirhams, back to the seller for dinars. Their proof has passed earlier: for Abu Yusuf, iqalah being sale is the principle; for Muhammad, the principle is rescission, but since rescission is impossible due to mentioning a different type, it is considered a sale because that is possible. The author of al-Hidayah said: If the slave-girl gives birth after the buyer took possession, then the parties make iqalah, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this iqalah is void. The proof is that according to him, iqalah is only rescission. After possession, an increase that is separate from the sale prevents rescission, and the child is a separate increase, so it prevents rescission. When rescission is prevented, iqalah becomes void, and the first sale remains as it was. But if the slave-girl gives birth before the buyer took possession, then according to Imam the iqalah is valid because a separate increase before possession does not prevent rescission. And if the sold item becomes fat (increases), this increase does not prevent rescission either before or after possession. The Sahibayn said that if iqalah is made after the slave-girl gives birth, this iqalah is a sale: for Abu Yusuf because iqalah being a sale is the principle; for Muhammad because when rescission is impossible due to the separate increase, iqalah is made a sale because that is possible. Before explaining the passage of the author of al-Hidayah, 'And iqalah before delivery for movables...' etc., note that sale of movables before delivery is unanimously impermissible. And sale of immovables like land and house before delivery is permissible according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) but impermissible according to Imam Muhammad. Now the meaning of the passage is: If the sold item is movable or immovable, and the buyer makes iqalah without taking possession, then according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) this iqalah is a rescission of the sale, because for them the principle is that iqalah is rescission. And according to Abu Yusuf also, if the sale is of a movable, iqalah is rescission because sale is impossible, so he treats it as rescission. And if the sold item is immovable and the buyer makes iqalah before possession, according to Abu Yusuf this iqalah is a sale because sale is possible, since according to him sale of immovables before delivery is permissible. (From Minyah al-Hidayah)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings on iqalah. First, it addresses iqalah with a different type of price (e.g., dirhams to dinars). Abu Hanifa maintains it as rescission with the original price, ignoring the new specification. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a new sale because rescission is impossible. Second, it discusses iqalah when the sold slave-girl gives birth. Abu Hanifa voids the iqalah because the child is a separate increase that prevents rescission; the Sahibayn treat it as a sale. Third, it examines iqalah before delivery. For movables, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is rescission; Abu Yusuf agrees because sale of movables before delivery is invalid. For immovables, Abu Yusuf treats iqalah as a sale because sale of immovables before delivery is allowed in his view. The detailed Urdu commentary clarifies these points, emphasizing that the ruling depends on whether rescission is possible or not, and the different positions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
اقالة (iqalah): Mutual rescission of a sale contract; both parties agree to cancel the transaction.
جنس (jins): Type or category, here referring to the type of currency or price (e.g., dirhams vs dinars).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling of iqalah when the price type is changed (e.g., from dirhams to dinars)?
A) It is a valid rescission; the original price must be returned.
B) It is a new sale with the new price type.
C) It is void because the price type must match.
D) It is a gift requiring acceptance.

Key Takeaway
In iqalah with a different price type, Abu Hanifa holds it as rescission with the original price; the Sahibayn consider it a new sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Iqalah After the Slave-Girl Gives Birth
Ruling on iqalah when the sold slave-girl gives birth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa voids iqalah when a sold slave-girl gives birth after delivery, while the Sahibayn treat it as a sale, and apply this reasoning to other separable increases.

Core Idea
A separable increase like childbirth prevents rescission; Abu Hanifa voids iqalah, Sahibayn make it a sale.

When the object of sale undergoes a physical change—such as a slave-girl giving birth—the possibility of simply 'returning' the item becomes complex. The Hanafi Imams differ on whether such a change allows the original sale to be rescinded by mutual agreement. This lesson dissects their reasoning on the effect of a separable increase (ziyada munfasila) on iqalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the increase
Recognize that the birth of a child is a separable increase (i.e., can be separated from the mother). This matters because it changes the composition of the sold item.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa rules that iqalah after birth is void because the child is a separate increase that prevents rescission of the original sale.
3
State the Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn rule that the iqalah becomes a sale: the buyer sells the slave-girl and her child back to the seller for the original price.
4
Analyze the reasoning
For Abu Hanifa, iqalah is only rescission; a separable increase makes rescission impossible because the sold item is no longer the same. For the Sahibayn, since rescission is impossible, the iqalah is re-characterized as a new sale.
5
Distinguish before and after possession
Note that if the birth occurs before the buyer takes possession, Abu Hanifa allows iqalah because a separable increase before possession does not prevent rescission.

Ruling of iqalah with a different type than the original price. 'And if he cancels (iqalah) with other than the type of the first price, then it is a rescission based on the first price according to Abu Hanifa, and the naming (of the other type) is considered void. And according to them (Sahibayn), it is a sale, as we have established. And if the sold female slave gives birth to a child, then they make iqalah, the iqalah is void according to him (Abu Hanifa) because the child prevents rescission. And according to them, it would be a sale. And iqalah before delivery, for movable property and other than it, is rescission according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and similarly according to Abu Yusuf for movables, due to the impossibility of sale. And for immovables, according to him, iqalah is a sale because sale is possible, for sale of immovables before delivery is permissible according to him.' Translation: And if iqalah is made with a different type than the first price, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is a rescission based on the first price, and the mention of the other type is considered void. And according to the Sahibayn, this iqalah is a sale due to the proof we mentioned. And if a slave-girl gives birth to a child, then both make iqalah, the iqalah is void according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) because the child prevents rescission. And according to the Sahibayn, it would be a sale. And iqalah before delivery for movables and other things is rescission according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and similarly according to Abu Yusuf for movables because sale is impossible. And for immovables, according to him, iqalah is a sale because sale is possible, for according to Abu Yusuf sale of immovables before delivery is permissible. (Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Sharh of Hidayah, Volume 8) Explanation: The case is that if iqalah is made with a different type than the first price, e.g., the first price was dirhams and iqalah is made with dinars, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this iqalah is a rescission of the sale based on the first price (dirhams), and the mention of dinars is void. That is, the seller must return the first price (dirhams), not the dinars. According to the Sahibayn, this iqalah is a sale with the other type, i.e., it will be said that the buyer sold the item, which he had bought for dirhams, back to the seller for dinars. Their proof has passed earlier: for Abu Yusuf, iqalah being sale is the principle; for Muhammad, the principle is rescission, but since rescission is impossible due to mentioning a different type, it is considered a sale because that is possible. The author of al-Hidayah said: If the slave-girl gives birth after the buyer took possession, then the parties make iqalah, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this iqalah is void. The proof is that according to him, iqalah is only rescission. After possession, an increase that is separate from the sale prevents rescission, and the child is a separate increase, so it prevents rescission. When rescission is prevented, iqalah becomes void, and the first sale remains as it was. But if the slave-girl gives birth before the buyer took possession, then according to Imam the iqalah is valid because a separate increase before possession does not prevent rescission. And if the sold item becomes fat (increases), this increase does not prevent rescission either before or after possession. The Sahibayn said that if iqalah is made after the slave-girl gives birth, this iqalah is a sale: for Abu Yusuf because iqalah being a sale is the principle; for Muhammad because when rescission is impossible due to the separate increase, iqalah is made a sale because that is possible. Before explaining the passage of the author of al-Hidayah, 'And iqalah before delivery for movables...' etc., note that sale of movables before delivery is unanimously impermissible. And sale of immovables like land and house before delivery is permissible according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) but impermissible according to Imam Muhammad. Now the meaning of the passage is: If the sold item is movable or immovable, and the buyer makes iqalah without taking possession, then according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) this iqalah is a rescission of the sale, because for them the principle is that iqalah is rescission. And according to Abu Yusuf also, if the sale is of a movable, iqalah is rescission because sale is impossible, so he treats it as rescission. And if the sold item is immovable and the buyer makes iqalah before possession, according to Abu Yusuf this iqalah is a sale because sale is possible, since according to him sale of immovables before delivery is permissible. (From Minyah al-Hidayah)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings on iqalah. First, it addresses iqalah with a different type of price (e.g., dirhams to dinars). Abu Hanifa maintains it as rescission with the original price, ignoring the new specification. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a new sale because rescission is impossible. Second, it discusses iqalah when the sold slave-girl gives birth. Abu Hanifa voids the iqalah because the child is a separate increase that prevents rescission; the Sahibayn treat it as a sale. Third, it examines iqalah before delivery. For movables, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is rescission; Abu Yusuf agrees because sale of movables before delivery is invalid. For immovables, Abu Yusuf treats iqalah as a sale because sale of immovables before delivery is allowed in his view. The detailed Urdu commentary clarifies these points, emphasizing that the ruling depends on whether rescission is possible or not, and the different positions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
زيادة منفصلة (ziyada munfasila): A separable increase in the sold item, such as a child born to a slave-girl or fruit on a tree.
مانع الفسخ (mani' al-faskh): Barrier to rescission; something that makes it impossible to return the sold item in its original state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is iqalah void if a sold slave-girl gives birth after the buyer's possession?
A) Because the buyer did not intend to purchase a mother.
B) Because the child is a separable increase that prevents rescission.
C) Because the seller did not consent to sell the child.
D) Because the iqalah must be in the same currency.

Key Takeaway
A separable increase after possession blocks rescission in iqalah according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn convert it into a sale.
